Japan Building Five Major Railways in the Northeast 34

(Beiping) After the Japanese took control of the Northeast, in addition to completing the Duntuo Railway and building the Anlong Laha Yanha Road, they also ordered the South Manchuria Railway Company to build five major railways: (1) Liaore Line: Shenyang to Chengde; (2) Hatao Line: Harbin to Taonan; (3) Tangsui Line: Tangyuan to Suihua; (4) Jitong Line: Jilin to Tongjiang; (5) Qihei Line: Qike to Heihe. The above five major railways are all of great military significance and are currently under active construction. After the five routes are completed, the Japanese army will be able to mobilize quickly, eliminate the volunteer army, and control our side. (31st Day Special Dispatch)

Japan Prepares to Cope with the Second Washington Conference 42

Deeply Afraid of Discussions on the Manchuria Problem

Hull Issues Another Statement to Japan

(Nanjing) The Army authorities are very concerned because of the possibility that the Manchuria problem will be raised as an issue at next year's Washington Conference. (1) It is quite clear that China, based on its traditional policy and the relationship of the problem with the Nine-Power Treaty nations, will exhaust all means to raise it as an issue at the conference. (2) Judging from the fact that Japan withdrew from the League of Nations due to the Manchuria problem and the current trade pressure against Japan, the countries participating in the conference are expected to be more sympathetic to China than at the 1921 Washington Conference. (3) Not only the League of Nations member states but also countries around the world recognize that Japan's attitude during the Manchurian Incident violated the Nine-Power Treaty signed at the First Washington Conference. Even from a theoretical point of view, China's appeal cannot be rejected. Therefore, the Army authorities anticipate the above as important bases for the possibility of raising the Manchuria problem at next year's Washington Conference. Currently, they are earnestly studying countermeasures on how to deal with it. Soon, they will propose to the Second Washington Conference Countermeasures Consultative Council of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Navy, Army, and other related authorities, which will be established soon, and strongly assert it. As for the opinions among the authorities in charge, it has been decided as follows: No matter how sweet the words or fine language used to encourage the Manchuria problem to be an issue at the conference, if it is agreed, it will directly hinder the development of "Manchukuo" and disrupt peace in East Asia. Therefore, it must be resolutely rejected. For this reason, the inviting country should be independently inquired beforehand as to whether the issue is on the agenda. If it is confirmed that the issue is not on the agenda, but it is suddenly raised after participating in the conference, the Japanese delegation may withdraw immediately. (31st Day Electric News)

(Washington) The American business community requested the State Department to designate March 31st as "Admiral Perry" Memorial Day to commemorate the first signing of the Japan-US Treaty of Amity and Commerce (i.e., the Treaty of Kanagawa) between US Admiral Perry and the Japanese government on March 31, 1854. Secretary of State Hull has recently accepted. Hull issued a statement on this issue today, stating, "The treaty signed by Admiral Perry laid the foundation for the establishment of relations between Japan and the United States, upon which the two countries' consolidated friendship and mutual interests were built. The relationship between the United States and Japan is similar today to what it was eighty years ago, based on friendship, and this is true not only for Japan but also for other countries." Hull continued, "The United States and Japan are also following the same path in industry and commerce, not harming each other but seeking the common welfare of mankind," and so on. Before 1854, Japan pursued a policy of national isolation, discriminating against foreigners. It was not until this year that US Admiral Perry led a fleet to Japan, knocking on the door and entering. At that time, Japan had no strong armor or sharp weapons and knew that it was powerless to resist. Therefore, it began to sign the Treaty of Kanagawa with the Americans, opening up maritime trade. (30th Day Havas Dispatch)

(New York) A bulletin issued today by the British Foreign Policy Association stated that the documents recently exchanged between Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota and US Secretary of State Hull did not indicate that the United States had changed its policy of non-recognition of "Manchukuo." League of Nations Fears Far East Problem Will Lead to Second World War 43

Japan Dominates East Asian Situation

Britain and America May Cooperate to Deal with It

(Geneva) The League of Nations believes that if urgent steps are not taken to ease the tension in the Far East, a second world war may not be far off. According to sources within the League of Nations, the first countries to participate in the war would be Japan, the Soviet Union, and China, and Britain and the United States would inevitably be drawn into the vortex sooner or later. The League of Nations' prediction is based on its study of the causes of war. Geneva predicts the main reasons for the war as follows:

(1) The United States, China, and Russia will resist Japan's attempt to create political and commercial hegemony in the Far East.

(2) Japan's actions in Manchuria undermine the balance of power stipulated by the Washington Naval Conference of 1922.

(3) Due to Japan's intention to demand naval parity at the future naval conference to be held in 1935, the naval construction competition between Japan and the United States will intensify.

(4) Relations between Japan and Russia are gradually entering a turbulent period, as can be seen from the recent strong attitude expressed by the Soviet Union.

(5) The expansion of Japan's foreign trade and Japan's insistence on the Asia Monroe Doctrine have made Britain deeply uneasy.

(6) China refuses to recognize the Japanese-controlled "Manchukuo," which was originally China's Northeast Three Provinces.

(7) Japan formally declared its withdrawal from the League of Nations in 1935, and Japan declared its continued trusteeship of a majority of islands.

Observers predict that an accident will inevitably occur in Japanese-Russian relations this spring. Tokyo and England are also creating an atmosphere of war, and conflicts on the border between the two countries may cause an accident. According to experts familiar with the Far East situation, Japan must abandon its Monroe policy in the Far East, but Japan is unwilling to do so. Therefore, the only result is that Japan and Russia will meet with soldiers. The outcome of the war is, of course, closely related to the United States. If Japan wins, the United States must decide whether to participate in the war or retreat, and let Japan monopolize the interests of the Far East and China. According to the League of Nations, the United States has not yet decided on its steps in this matter, but as a precaution, the United States has decided to strengthen its navy to the extent permitted by the treaty. Most well-informed observers believe that the US military in the US plan will never have the opportunity to fight against Japan, because the Washington government will eventually carefully consider the cost and benefits of the war. However, this is tantamount to the United States recognizing Japan's position as the master of the Far East, and abandoning China's open door policy from now on. Most diplomats believe that the United States will eventually swallow its anger and withdraw from the Far East, so as to concentrate on the development of politics and commerce in Latin America. If the United States does not need to make an urgent decision this year, the United States will eventually have to decide on its policy at the naval conference in 1935 at the latest. According to diplomats in Geneva, the foundation of the United States' Far East policy has been completely destroyed by Japan's atrocities in Manchuria. In other words, all Pacific treaties similar in nature to the Washington Naval Treaty are now regarded as waste paper. It is said that the Nine-Power Treaty has been undermined, because the signatory countries have no way to deal with Japan's infringement of China's sovereignty and territory. Japan's actions in Manchuria have been victorious, so Japan has become the master of the Asian continent, and the balance of power in the Far East presided over by the Washington Treaty has been destroyed. Furthermore, in order to maintain its new position in the Pacific, Japan is now requesting naval parity from Britain and the United States. The League of Nations is deeply afraid that if Japan's demands cannot be satisfied, there will be no hope of re-signing a new treaty after the expiration of the London and Washington treaties, and the inevitable result will be naval competition, but the cost will be incalculable. In the same uneasy area as the Far East Treaty structure is the intensification of economic competition in the Far East. Japan, through its own competitive efforts, feels the tension in its relations with other countries, especially Britain. Japan's victory in seizing foreign markets and Japan's competition with Britain on maritime routes have made Britain unable to forget the Far East. Some parties believe that Britain and the United States may cooperate to promote Japan's awareness, so as to avoid bloodshed and war. (30th National Telegraph)

Russian Army Mechanized 44

Tank Manufacturing Self-Sufficient

Results of the Five-Year Industrial Plan

Moscow News, The Soviet Army is making every effort to mechanize and modernize its troops. The peacetime strength of its tank force is roughly as follows: 4 tank regiments, 3 independent tank companies, 6 independent tank battalions, 2 independent tank companies of security force divisions, 6 independent tank companies, and 8 tank companies attached to sniper divisions. The regiment consists of 2 light tank battalions, 1 heavy tank battalion (each battalion is composed of 3 companies formed by heavy and light platoons), and an education battalion (1 heavy and 1 light company). The platoon was originally 3 tanks, and is currently being reorganized into 5 tanks. In addition to focusing on the enrichment of the tank force, the Soviet army is also keen to build mechanized troops to ensure various services. The mechanized vehicles necessary for this type of troop have always been supplied by imports. Recently, as a result of the five-year industrial plan focusing on the development of domestic heavy industry, the development of automobiles has shown a significant trend. In 1931, the domestic factory's tank manufacturing volume was approximately 500 vehicles. At present, the tank force of the Soviet Far East forces is approximately 300 vehicles east of Chita. Results After the Implementation of the Ottawa Agreement 49

British Empire Trade Still Has Not Improved

However, as a whole, British Empire trade has not expanded significantly. After the general situation improves, the Ottawa policy will definitely have good results, which can be seen from the trends in early 1934. In 1933, the import of goods from other countries within the British Empire to the United Kingdom totaled £249,450,000, an increase of £1,300,000 compared with 1932. The export of British goods to other countries within the Empire totaled £163,000,000, a decrease of £2,000,000 compared with 1932. The reason why imperial trade has failed to respond to the encouragement of the Ottawa policy is that British trade with South Ireland and Hong Kong has decreased significantly. Capital of Yugoslavia Around the 15th of this month, it was rumored that two trains full of military supplies crossed Austria on March 8 and 9 and were transported to Hungary. This news will be published by the "Political News of the Southern Capital" tomorrow. The main points are: "On March 9, a train arrived at Sangandito on the Italian-Austrian border, with 18 freight cars, 4 of which belonged to Austria and 14 to Italy. The Austrian freight cars were covered with canvas. When they arrived in the Lin area, the cloth covering the cars was replaced. It is not known what was hidden inside. In the other Italian freight cars, the upper layer was covered with cauliflower, but someone saw that under the cauliflower, there were four armored military vehicles and various military uniforms. After this train entered Austria, it first stopped near Vienna. It is not known whether it was transferred to Hungary or stayed in Austria. In Klaz and Praina, military transport was also discovered. Ten days ago, 15 aircraft flown by Italian pilots flew to Darlehof in Austria. Afterwards, the Italian pilots all returned home by train. The aircraft were manufactured by the "Fiat" factory (a famous Italian manufacturer of automobiles and aircraft), with 750 horsepower. Aircraft parts were also transported at the same time, 12 of which were equipped with machine guns. Italy has supplied 48 aircraft to Hungary." (30th Havas News Agency)

Residents of Bucharest were awakened from their dreams, and most of them did not have time to change their pajamas before fleeing to the streets. The audience at the Bucharest Grand Theater rushed out of the doors in advance because the building was shaking, causing many people to be trampled. In other places, houses collapsed and injured people. During the earthquake, there was a sound like thunder from the ground, which increased the panic of the residents. The number of deaths and injuries is currently unknown, and the property losses have not been ascertained, but it is known that the number is not small. Government offices in various places are now engaged in clearing rubble and searching for corpses. Volunteer rescue teams have been organized in various cities, and the Romanian government is also trying to provide relief to homeless victims. (30th Reuters News Agency)

(Moscow) Last night, there were multiple earthquakes throughout southern Russia. Buildings and furniture shook quite violently in Kiev. (30th Reuters News Agency)

Development of Catholicism in China 59

Vatican City, Rome According to a report received by the Vatican from the Catholic representative in Beiping, the number of Catholics in China in the past ten years is 5,501,111. The number of children of spring believers is not included. It is said that there are currently 2,624,116 Catholics in China. In the past ten years, the number of foreign bishops who came to China has increased from 1,500 to 2,346. The number of Chinese bishops has increased from 118 to 1,614. The rate of increase in believers is 16%. The number of students in Catholic churches in China is 2,088, 3,419 in elementary schools, 813 in middle schools, and 243 who are studying philosophy and theology for religious and social use. There are 41 students studying in Rome and 9 studying in other countries. (30th National Telegraph)

Stockholm, Sweden – Just weeks after the second grandson of the Swedish King relinquished his royal rights by marrying a German businesswoman, Cupid has struck the Swedish royal family once more. (Nanjing) – Ai Chengmei, the first wife of Gu Renfa, resided in San Tiao Xiang, Drum Tower, in Nanjing. Since the Gu-Li affair occurred, she had intended to hire a lawyer to sue Gu for bigamy. According to the Criminal Procedure Law, a lawsuit against a husband for bigamy must be filed in the court of the defendant's location or where the crime was committed. Fu Zhan魁 Talks About Persuading Sun Dianying to Step Down 102

Sun Initially Had No Determination to Attack Ningxia

Officers and Soldiers All Wept Upon His Departure

Fu's Trip Was Also Full of Difficulties

Beiping Correspondence - Fu Zhan魁, who was tasked with persuading Sun Dianying to step down a month ago, spared no effort and trudged through the Hetao Desert, experiencing several days of food and water shortage. He finally completed his mission with perseverance and returned to Beiping on the 27th. Sun Dianying was originally traveling with Fu, but at about 1:00 AM on the morning of the 27th, while passing through Datong, Yang Aiyuan, commander of the 34th Army garrisoning Taiyuan, dispatched by Yan Xishan, welcomed Sun to Jin on behalf of Yan. Sun got off the train at that place. After meeting with Yan in Jin and making arrangements for his family, he will choose a day to come to Beiping and send his Secretary-General Liu Zenruo with a letter from Sun to Fu to pay respects to Chairman He and Sun's friends in Beiping to thank them for their kindness in maintaining the army. Fu and Liu arrived in Beiping at 4:30 PM on the 27th. Many of Fu's friends and Sun's former subordinates came to welcome them at the station. According to Fu's account of the journey,

"Sun is a man of generosity and righteousness, and he values promises. The conflict with the Ningxia army was unexpected. After the engagement, the two armies were in a stalemate, making it impossible to stop. After receiving the central government's order to stop advancing westward, Sun immediately intended to withdraw his troops. However, the two armies were in a stalemate, and it was necessary to consider the safety of his subordinates. The central government did not explicitly order the Ningxia army to abandon its intention to fight Sun, so Sun repeatedly asked the central government and the Military Affairs Commission to send senior officials to the front line to monitor and prevent the Ningxia army from pursuing Sun. Under the guidance of the senior monitoring officials, Sun obeyed the order and retreated backward. In the middle of this, the senior monitoring officials were delayed in being dispatched, so the retreat of Sun's troops was also delayed, and there were unavoidable clashes between the two sides during this period. Commander Pang and others, due to friendly relations, sent a telegram to Sun with gentle advice. After receiving Sun's reply, I (referring to himself) was asked to meet with Sun. Chairman He also believed that a military solution would inevitably harm the local area and also agreed with me going to persuade Sun to step down. I know Sun well, so I went on a mission despite the hardships. The traffic in the Hetao area is extremely inconvenient. South of Dengkou, it takes three days of travel, and there is not a single village along the way, making progress extremely difficult. The round trip took a month, with twenty days spent walking.

I met Sun on the 10th of this month in Ligangbao. After Sun saw me, he immediately expressed his sincerity without any doubts or demands. Everything was done in accordance with the orders of the Military Affairs Commission. The tens of thousands of officers and soldiers of the department were all trained by Sun, and they shared hardships together for more than ten years. Although Sun is a military commander, his enjoyment is the same as that of the soldiers. Therefore, in his army, the relationship is like that of family and fathers and sons. This time Sun resolutely resigned, and the entire army was reluctant to part with him. When Sun set off, the officers and soldiers all wailed and cried. Sun and the officers met each other before departure and cried bitterly all night. I was on the sidelines and also felt the pain of separation more than death. Under such a passionate environment, Sun resolutely gave up, which is truly admirable. Sun's generosity and righteousness are well known. This time he left the army, he did not have a single penny on him, nor did he ask the government for money. In order to appease the families of his subordinates, he specially telegraphed his friends in Beiping a few days ago to mortgage all his private property in Beiping to borrow 24,000 yuan to send to Baotou. For each family of those who had dependents left in the area, 20 yuan was given to each family. 17,000 yuan was distributed in one night. The remaining 7,000 yuan was also distributed to the officers who came with him. The officers strongly kept 2,000 yuan for Sun to use, but as a result of the distribution, 5,000 yuan was still not enough to distribute everywhere, so Sun took out his 2,000 yuan and distributed it again. As far as I know, Sun has absolutely less than 500 yuan in his hands. For more than ten years, his subordinates have suffered hardships and followed him because of Sun's righteousness.

My mission was only to persuade Sun to step down, so I did not ask about the military tunnel. Wang Zhongquan and Zhang Xuanze, two staff officers from the Military Affairs Commission who went with me, have stayed on the front line to monitor the centralized reorganization of Sun's troops. The Military Affairs Commission ordered the department to withdraw north of Shizuishan to await reorganization, but there is nowhere to stay in the 200-odd li between Shizuishan and Dengkou. If they want to withdraw north, they must withdraw to Dengkou. In fact, they cannot stop south of Dengkou. Ding Futing's troops are now 15 li outside Ningxia City, while Liu Yueting and others are gathering near Shizuishan. Transportation in the Hetao area is extremely inconvenient. The journey took many days. Telegrams took three or four days to arrive. Since the 41st Army was disbanded, the Military Affairs Commission's radio station does not receive telegrams from the army, so they must be forwarded from Taiyuan or Chairman Fu, so there are fewer telegrams.

The journey this time was as follows: On the 4th of this month, I set off from Baotou and arrived in Wuyuan in the evening. On the 5th, I arrived in Linhe. On the 6th, I arrived in Sanshenggong. On the 7th, I arrived in Dengkou. The car could no longer be used, so I switched to sedan chairs and horses to travel on the canals and small paths and in the desert. I only traveled dozens of li a day. On the 8th, I arrived in Heguazi, which is the bend of the Yellow River. On the 9th, I arrived in Shizuishan. On the 10th, I arrived in Ligangbao. I had to pass outside Pingluo City and was still shot at by the garrison in the city. I telegraphed Sun my itinerary every day on the way. As soon as I arrived, Sun also rushed from Zhengjia Oil Mill. After seeing each other, he immediately decided to leave the army with me. However, because he was dealing with matters in the military headquarters, and I was waiting for a telegram from the Military Affairs Commission, I started to move first on the 16th. I arrived in Dengkou by car on the 18th. In order to avoid passing through Pingluo, Sun rode a horse to catch up. I received a telegram from Sun on the 19th, inviting me to travel with him in Dengkou. He rode slower, arriving on the morning of the 22nd. Then we traveled south together. I met Wang Jingguo in Sanshenggong, saw Fu Zuoyi and Zhao Chengshou in Linhe, and only stayed in Baotou for one day. This time when I returned, I saw that the canals in Hetao had thawed and the water was rising. If I was not careful, I would fall into the canal. There were four days on the way when I did not eat hot meals, but only filled my stomach with dry food. I dared not drink water for three days. The water there is more turbid than the water in the drains of Beiping, and the shores are full of dead camels and excrement. I really dare not drink it." (28th)

Expanding the Organization 103

Appointment of Personnel for Two Departments and Six Sections Already Determined Internally

Party Affairs Funds for Three Provinces Still Disbursed from Provincial Treasury

Hankou Correspondence: Since Commander-in-Chief Chiang relocated his headquarters to Nanchang, the General Headquarters of the Commander-in-Chief for Bandit Suppression in Henan, Hubei, and Anhui Provinces has been managed by Chief of Staff Cao Haosen and Qian Dajun, who successively acted on his behalf. When Zhang Xueliang took office as Deputy Commander-in-Chief, he assumed full responsibility. Zhang took office on March 1st and went to Jiangxi on the 7th to meet with Chiang. In addition to discussing post-bandit suppression measures and the deployment of various military defenses, it is said that they also discussed the issue of expanding the General Headquarters' organization. On the 13th, Zhang returned to Hankou from Jiangxi and went to the General Headquarters every day at 8:00 AM to work. The organization of the General Headquarters has been decided to be expanded, roughly divided into the First and Second Departments and six major sections. It is said that the personnel appointments have already been internally determined and are planned to be implemented on April 1st. Zhang's Yamen will be moved from Hankou to the East Garden of Xujiapeng in Wuchang, which has now been renovated and will be moved into soon, making it more convenient to work at the General Headquarters in the future. The Hankou Yamen will still be converted into an office. Zhang is making great efforts to rectify internal staff, immediately planning to establish a "General Headquarters New Life Movement Promotion Association," leading by example and setting an example for the military and political organs of the three provinces. An English class will also be established, stipulating that staff practice Tai Chi from 8:00 AM to 9:00 AM, study English from 1:00 PM to 2:00 PM, and practice soccer, tennis, and basketball after 5:00 PM, in order to enhance their knowledge and improve their physical and mental health.

The General Headquarters previously issued a summary of Party affairs reorganization in the three provinces, stipulating that the expenses of the provincial Party headquarters of the three provinces and the Hankou Special City Party headquarters should be self-sufficient from Party members from the 23rd year onwards and no longer drawn from the provincial treasury. Because it has not been done during the bandit suppression period, on the 29th, Commander-in-Chief Chiang telegraphed Zhang Xueliang and the governments of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, ordering that they still be disbursed from the provincial treasury according to the original plan. The original telegram said, "Deputy Commander Zhang in Wuchang, Chairman Zhang, Chairman Liu in Kaifeng, Chairman Liu in Anqing, I have reviewed Article 10 of the Provisional Outline for the Reorganization of Party Affairs in the Bandit Suppression Area promulgated by this Headquarters, which originally stipulated that the expenses of the provincial Party headquarters and the special city Party headquarters should quickly plan for self-sufficiency, and after the 22nd year, they should no longer be disbursed from the provincial treasury. Now, according to the Central Party Headquarters Secretariat's respectful telegram, the Central Finance Committee meeting stated that during this bandit suppression period in the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, Party affairs are important, and the expenses of the provincial and municipal Party headquarters are still difficult to handle on their own for a while. In the 23rd year, the Party affairs expenses of the three provinces should still be transferred to the three provincial governments to include them in the budget as before, in order to maintain the status quo, etc. What is said is still true. Recently, the Jiangxi Provincial Government also asked whether the provincial Party affairs expenses for the 23rd year should be listed as before, and I have instructed that they should still be temporarily included in the budget. The matter of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui is the same example. In addition to replying to the Central Secretariat, I hope that they will be temporarily included in the budget separately. Signed by Chiang Kai-shek." (March 30th)

Chiang Orders Three Provinces to Completely Eradicate Remnant Bandits within a Time Limit 104

He, Liu, and Others Meet with Zhang in Hankou to Discuss Post-Affairs

Zhang Fang Telegraphed that Bandit Leader Ma Xiyou Had Been Killed in Action

Hankou Correspondence: Liu Zhenhua, Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in the Border Area of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, went to Jiangxi a few days ago to meet with Chiang and report on the bandit situation in the border area. He then came to Hankou on the 28th in response to a telegram from Deputy Commander Zhang. On the 29th, he met with Zhang once and discussed the post-bandit suppression plan and troop command matters. On the same day, Chairman Chiang telegraphed Liu and various generals, ordering them to completely eradicate the remaining bandits in the border area, only Wu Huanxian and Xu Haidong, with a total number of no more than three thousand people, within one month, seeking to annihilate them as soon as possible. After Liu led the order, he went to the Yamen again on the 30th with He Chengjun, the Pacification Commissioner stationed in Hubei, to meet with Deputy Commander Zhang and discuss everything in detail. Chief of Staff Qian Dajun of the General Headquarters also participated in the meeting to decide on the methods for carrying out post-bandit suppression. Liu plans to go to the border area to inspect in a few days, and then return to Liuan to supervise the suppression. Various division commanders, such as Liu Maoen and Dai Minquan, originally planned to come to Hankou and Jiangxi to meet with Chiang and Zhang for instructions, but because of the deployment of military affairs, they all stopped leaving their defenses. Sun Lianzhong, who came to Hankou, has already gone to Jiangxi the day before, and Liang Guanying will also go. It is said that a certain unit in the border area has recently joined the suppression, and the elimination of the remaining bandits is not a problem. As for the ten bandits in southern Henan and northern Hubei, Wang You and Ma Xiyou, etc., who fled to western Henan, Zhang Fang is supervising the troops to pursue and suppress them. Zhang telegraphed Director He Chengjun on the 29th to report the victory, saying, "According to a telegram from Deputy Division Commander Li Qin (27th), the bandits Ma and Wang were severely attacked by our 453rd Regiment and artillery battalion in Xindian on the 24th. The bandits fled east from Bao'an. On the 25th, they went to the southern end of Liudian, where our engineering battalion was opening to the south, and engaged in a battle for two hours, killing and wounding dozens of bandits. They turned north and fled to the Zhaocun area north of Jiuxian. Our artillery and engineering battalions followed and pursued them. At 10:00 PM that night, taking advantage of the bandits' fatigue, they bravely rushed in and engaged in hand-to-hand combat for two hours, killing more than 200 bandits, capturing more than a dozen alive, and seizing 43 rifles and 47 mules and horses. After the battle, the bandits unexpectedly gathered their remnants and launched a counterattack on three sides. The attack was extremely fierce. After another four hours of fierce fighting, the deputy of our artillery battalion and dozens of officers and soldiers were killed and wounded. The bandits still could not hold on and fled southwest. According to the captured bandits, the reason for the desperate counterattack was that the bandit leader Ma Xiyou was killed in this battle and they were trying to get his body, etc. Now our 453rd and 456th Regiments and artillery and engineering battalions have all reached Yexian. According to reconnaissance reports, the remnant bandits have fled to the Weiwa area southwest of Baofeng, but today there is a heavy snow, making it difficult to advance, etc. In addition to ordering the inspection of the corpse of bandit Ma Xiyou, I have also ordered them to follow and pursue the bandits to ensure that they are all annihilated." (March 30th)

Recent Situation of Military and Political Affairs in Fujian Province 105

The Provincial Government Plans to Implement Important Policies

Various Military Shortages Ordered to be Replenished

Fuzhou Correspondence: The bandit suppression military affairs in Fujian Province have been very smooth recently, but in terms of politics, due to financial difficulties, there has been no progress. The provincial government recently received a telegram from Chairman Chiang ordering it to actively carry out four important policies: measuring land, checking household registration, establishing Baojia, and building highways, in order to complete the task of advancing both bandit suppression military affairs and politics, and setting a deadline of April to prepare detailed plans and submit them for approval, to be started in May and completed by the end of April next year. After receiving the order, the provincial government immediately summoned the heads of the civil affairs, construction, and finance departments, as well as the section chiefs and secretaries of the security office, to hold a joint meeting at the provincial government on the morning of March 28th. Secretary-General Gao Dengting chaired the meeting to discuss the implementation methods and decided: (1) Land measurement will be handled jointly by the civil affairs and finance departments, with the civil affairs department drafting the plan. (2) Household registration will be checked by the civil affairs department. (3) Baojia will be established jointly by the security office and the civil affairs department, with the security office drafting the plan. (4) Highways will be built by the construction department. The draft plan for each item should be divided into three parts: overview, steps, and expenses, and should be prepared before April 15th and submitted to the provincial government for review. The important policies recently handled by the provincial government include the case of setting up administrative commissioners in different regions, which has already drafted regulations for the commissioner's office, and the compilation of the estimated budget for the 23rd year, which can be completed by the end of March and must be submitted for discussion at the provincial government meeting on April 4th.

In terms of military affairs, the national army stationed in Fujian has already been dispatched by the Nanchang headquarters to send Cai Jilun and Kong Jianchang to Fujian to form an inspection committee with the East Road General Headquarters, divided into two groups, southern Fujian and northern Fujian, to start the inspection. However, the 39th Army under Liu Heding is newly established and only has jurisdiction over the 56th Division (Liu also concurrently serves as division commander), the 52nd Division under Lu Xingbang, the newly編 10th Division under Zhou Ziqun, the newly編 11th Division under Chen Zhaixuan, and the newly編

Page 12

The two師under Zhang Luanji have only one brigade each and have many vacancies. Now, according to the order of the Military Commission, all are allowed to expand their establishment. The method is to place the newly編 12th Division under the jurisdiction of the 39th Army, combining it with the original 56th Division of the army, for a total of two師. The four師under Lu Xingbang, Zhou Ziqun, Chen Zhaixuan, and Zhang Luanji will each be expanded by one regiment, combining the original three regiments to form four regiments, divided into two brigades. The candidates for brigade and regimental commanders can be announced within days. Inspection Record of Xinjiang by Our Newspaper's Special Correspondent, Geng Ya 106

Foreword

Since the outbreak of the September 18th Incident and the Japanese forcibly occupied our Northeast, the Chinese people have felt the urgency of the national crisis and have begun to look to the frontier areas. Therefore, the call to "develop the Northwest" has resounded across the clouds. Liang Rengong once said, "The fertile coastal areas are being devoured by tigers. In the event of war, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong will bear the brunt. In less than five years, all will be like Taiwan, abandoned in haste, and no cries will be heard. Even with strong weapons, they will only increase the enemy's food supply. Even with wisdom and courage, they will be helpless. Therefore, talking about wealth and strength while living in the southeast is like gorging oneself in front of a butcher's door. Although it is a little pleasant, one will never get meat. Only the northwest hinterland is far from the coast, with few foreign traces and undeveloped land. Greed comes a little later, and the abundance of mines and products, taking any province as an example, can all be self-sufficient." Zuo Zongtang also said, "Rebuilding Xinjiang is to protect Mongolia, and protecting Mongolia is to defend the capital. The northwest arms are connected, and the situation is complete, leaving no gap to be taken advantage of. If Xinjiang is not secure, Mongolia will not be safe. Not only will the borders of Shanxi and Shaanxi be threatened, but the mountains north of the capital will also have no peace." The northwest is our country's hall and treasury, and Xinjiang is especially the screen in the middle. Mongolia and Tibet are like lips and teeth. Reading the words of the two gentlemen can give a general idea. Moreover, Xinjiang was once a trading place for eastern and western civilizations, and in the future, it will reopen its meaning as a transportation route between Europe and Asia. The land is vast and the products are abundant, with an area of 4,947,700 square li, which is two-fifths of the area of the eighteen中部 provinces, one and a half times larger than Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang, fourteen times larger than Jiangsu Province, and fifteen times larger than Zhejiang Province. The population is 2,552,000 (according to the Ministry of the Interior in the 20th year), and the distribution density is an average of one person per two square li. Compared with the population density of Jiangsu Province, it is 190 times smaller, and 100 times smaller than Zhejiang. The more dense the population of the inland, the more impoverished the livelihood, while Xinjiang has vast land, fertile soil, and a sparse population, which makes it easy for foreigners to invade. In the 16th year, Hu Hanmin traveled in Europe and the Turkish Minister of Foreign Affairs asked Hu, "Why does China still ignore Xinjiang? If it is delayed any longer, Xinjiang will no longer belong to China." As we face the breaking of our rivers and mountains and the shrinking of our borders, we reread these words and cannot help but shudder. Now, in order to quickly mend the fold and do our respective duties, our newspaper has sent a special reporter to inspect Xinjiang, hoping to contribute to the people of the country with what we have learned, in order to have a clear understanding of the frontier situation and to promote the early realization of development plans, which I think will be welcomed by our beloved readers and supported by the people of the Northwest.

Leaving Shanghai to Go to Beijing to Obtain a Passport 107

According to the "Incentive Measures for Chinese Citizens to Investigate the Border" promulgated by the Ministry of the Interior in the spring of the 20th year, Chinese citizens who investigate the border, whether individually or in groups, should apply to the Ministry for an investigation passport. On February 22nd, the General Management Office of our newspaper submitted an investigation application, along with a half-length photo of the reporter, to our newspaper's Beijing office to apply for a passport. Because the procedures were incomplete, the application was returned and submitted to the Ministry of the Interior by the Shanghai Municipal Government. The reporter went to Beijing on March 6th to wait for the passport.

On the day of departure, I visited people from all walks of life who are very concerned about the Northwest issue. I was very grateful for their enlightenment and encouragement, which benefited me greatly. Li Zhichu (Du), a general of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Army, still affectionately remembered the soldiers stationed in the Northwest. He said that there had been no news from the remote area for three months and asked me to send a message, saying, "The Northeast has not been recovered, and Southern Xinjiang and Western Sichuan have also been troubled. Looking to the future, I am extremely worried. My comrades, survivors of the war, stationed in the Northwest, make people even more worried and restless. Recalling the past, the two places should have the same feelings. Now that the country is in trouble, all my comrades should still strive for the country with the spirit of resisting aggression. Du and his comrades should encourage each other." A fervent enthusiasm for worrying about the times and loving the country leaped onto the paper. That night at 12 o'clock, I departed on the Shanghai-Beijing through train from Shanghai North. The train was equipped with heating pipes, and despite the howling wind at night, there was no chill. The third-class seats were also very neat. There was also a small table under the window for drinking tea and writing. The first and second classes were even more comfortable, not to mention. This is enough to give passengers satisfaction. After arriving at Xiaguan, I got off the train and left the station. I saw a newly opened square, with a small garden planted with flowers and trees in the middle, and cars, carriages, and rickshaws lined up on the side. The order was still good, but the rickshaw pullers were very fierce in soliciting customers. If you take a so-called "wild chicken car" (the rickshaw puller claims it is a small car, to show the difference from a public bus), you can send four or five passengers to Xinjiekou or even the Confucius Temple for two dimes each. Taking other cars costs more. The area near the station, as well as the area from Rehe Road to Zhongshan Road to Xinjiekou, used to be dilapidated ruins, but now many have become magnificent government offices and tall 洋樓 banks. Other empty land and vegetable gardens are also planted with wooden signs saying "New Site of Bank XX" or "Construction by Construction Company XX". The atmosphere in Beijing is changing day by day, and the population is increasing sharply (from 250,000 to 726,000 since the capital was established). The banking industry is particularly developed, which can be seen generally.

The well water in Beijing is salty, and the price of river water is high and not clarified, so there is a lack of drinking water. Some people even ignore hygiene and draw water from ponds. Now the municipal government has established a government-run tap water system and set up 75 water stations in the busy street corners of the central and southern parts of the city. Each担of water (two 洋 oil barrels) costs three copper coins. The streets and alleys in the east and west of the city are narrow and inconvenient for laying water pipes, accounting for about half of the city. It is being gradually promoted and will soon be popularized. This is indeed beneficial to people's livelihood, and people praise it very much.

In recent years, government offices have been building extensively, and important people are competing to build villas, with flying eaves and beaded curtains, which is very spectacular and also a new show of the capital.

After unloading my luggage at the Datong Apartment, I visited the Ministry of the Interior and met Secretary Jiang Suishi. I asked about my passport and learned that it had not been forwarded because the procedures were not complete. I then sent a special letter to Li Dachao, the section chief of the Shanghai Municipal Government, asking him to expedite the inquiry. Later, I received a reply that it could be sent immediately. Then I visited Gong Bicheng, the director of the Xinjiang Provincial Office in Beijing. He received me cordially and said, "This trip is very meaningful and I highly approve of it. However, the situation in Xinjiang is slightly different from that in the interior. Before going to Xinjiang for investigation, you must first be investigated and approved by this office and telegraph the provincial government authorities. After receiving a welcome reply, you can enter the country unimpeded." I expressed my compliance to Mr. Gong and thanked him. Then I visited Wang Ruyi and Wang Shu, counselors of the National Government, Ma Hetian of the Ministry of Personnel of the Examination Yuan, Li Xiaochuan, a senator of the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs, Jiang Jingzhai, a section chief of the Ministry of Industry, and An Han, an executive member of the Northwest Construction Committee. We had in-depth discussions on the key points of the Northwest issue: (1) Developing the Northwest is the fundamental plan to save the country and the nation. Stabilizing Xinjiang is the first priority in developing the Northwest. (2) The crisis in Xinjiang today is no less than that in the Northeast before September 18th. (3) Xinjiang has a complex ethnic makeup. If it is lost, it will be more difficult to recover than the Northeast. (4) Those who aspire to work in the Northwest must have the same degree of philanthropic spirit as missionaries. They must not have the mentality of corrupt officials who exploit the people.

To investigate the border, you should have a passport. To go to Xinjiang, you must first apply to the authorities of the province for approval before you can travel. These procedures must be completed in advance to avoid delays and obstacles along the way. Now, I will extract the 17 articles of the "Measures for Rewarding Chinese Citizens for Investigating the Border" of the Ministry of the Interior as a warning to those who follow: (1) Anyone in this country who investigates the border (temporarily limited to Rehe, Chahar, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Gansu, Outer Mongolia, Xinjiang, Qinghai, Tibet, Xikang, Yunnan, and Guangxi), whether individually or in groups, must fill out three copies of the investigation application in the prescribed form, together with four 2-inch half-length photos, and send them to the local government for transfer to the Ministry of the Interior for review. (2) Students or professors of colleges above the specialty level may submit the application for investigation directly to the Ministry for processing by the president of the school where they are located. (3) If there is any doubt about the review, they may be ordered to come to the Ministry for an interview. Those who are far away may be questioned by the local government and reported. (4) If the review is approved, the Ministry will issue an investigation passport and a report form, and will notify the Ministry of Railways to issue a half-price train ticket. (5) After the Ministry issues an investigation passport, it shall immediately notify the administrative head of the border investigation area, and order his subordinates to protect and assist him. (6) When the investigator arrives at the border, he shall report to the local government, present his passport for verification, and report to the Ministry for verification. If he wishes to extend the investigation area or period during the investigation, he shall submit another application to the highest official in the border area for approval, and shall also report to the Ministry at the same time. (7) After the examination is completed, he shall submit the investigation situation and investigation opinions to the Ministry for review. If it is found that there are special achievements, he may apply for a reward.

The Story of Zeng Shangyuan, an Overseas Chinese Kidnapped in Xiamen, Escaping 108

Rescued by Garrison Troops in Tianzhu Mountain

Zeng Recounts His Kidnapping and Escape

Xiamen Correspondence: Zeng Shangyuan, a giant businessman in Xiamen who returned from Yangon and is the chairman of the Singapore Overseas Chinese Banking Corporation, was kidnapped on the night of March 17th on a ferry from Xiamen to Gulangyu. He was rescued on the 27th by the 36th Division of the Tong'an Garrison Troops near Tianzhu Mountain, at the border of Tong'an and Changtai. One of the bandits monitoring Zeng was asked by Zeng to carry Zeng's handwritten letter to Zeng's house in Gulangyu to report the news. Zeng's son, Yangwang, took the letter to Tong'an to report to the garrison troops to rescue him at the address. After Zeng escaped to Tong'an, he talked about his kidnapping and escape, saying, "I left the Daqian Hotel on the evening of the 17th. When I got on the ferry to Gulangyu, I saw two people in the boat first. I asked the helmsman Lin Tianguo and the driver Xu Hanguo who they were. They said they were their friends and wanted to take the boat to Gulangyu. I (Zeng said himself, hereinafter the same) thought they were Lin's own partners, so I didn't suspect them. In the middle of the river, I happened to look back and saw a small sampan being towed behind the ferry. I asked Lin again whose boat it was. Lin replied that it was his friend's boat, which was attached to carry passengers to Gulangyu. I was suspicious. Four people suddenly jumped out of the bottom of the sampan's cabin, all with weapons. I knew something was wrong. The four had already jumped over the ferry. One person stuffed my mouth with a bag of white powder and pointed a gun at my chest. At that time, the two people who were in the ferry first also took out guns, one monitoring the helmsman and one monitoring the driver. Then the electric boat went straight to Dalu Island between Songyu and Dongyu, passing the ship inspection office of the Water Police Bureau. The water police used a flashlight to shine on the ferry and asked where it was going. The bandits replied that it was going to Gulangyu. In fact, the route was absolutely inconsistent. If the water police had noticed that it did not match the direction and ordered it to approach for inspection, it might have been saved at that time. After passing the inspection ship office, the bandits fired a shot near Dalu Island and shattered the glass of the helmsman's room. This is the reason why there were bullet marks, bullet casings, and white powder in the empty boat that was later obtained. After arriving at Dalu Island, the bandits helped me ashore. More than 20 bandits were waiting. From there, they were taken to a thatched hut, where they lay dormant with the bandits for three days and nights, because Dalu Island is opposite Xiamen, fearing that the matter would be strictly monitored after it happened. On the morning of the 20th, I was moved to a sailboat. The bandits took two sailboats and set sail. At that time, the helmsman and driver Lin and Xu were not seen. The boat passed Bengpingwei in Yuandang Port, north of Xiamen City, and was stranded on the sandbar in front of the Asia Oil Depot due to low tide for a day. From morning to night, the Xiamen embankment and downtown area could be seen remotely. Unfortunately, no patrol boat arrived all day, so no one noticed that it was stranded on the shore of Xiamen all day long. When the tide rose in the evening, it continued to sail, passing Baozhu Island, and landing in Wu Guan. The mountains along the way to Xinyang Xiayang were rugged and difficult to walk. I was old (Zeng was 63 years old), exhausted and unable to support myself. During the past few days, they moved east and west, moving around in four places, all within the territory of Tong'an. Finally, they went to Tianzhu Mountain on the border of Tong'an and Changtai, the highest and most dangerous peak of the mountain, and lived there. At the time, one of the bandits said, 'Your helmsman and driver only know us and are not accomplices. If you go home one day, please don't make things difficult for them.' But I don't know if this is true. But judging from the past, the two are indeed suspicious. After living in the mountains for four days, four bandits guarded me day and night. One of the bandits was forced to become a bandit and had the intention of helping me. He said that his brother was a good citizen, had a family, and his property was worth 2,000 yuan. When I heard this, I thought I had a chance and asked him to ask his brother to be a liaison and told him that if he could escape, he would be rewarded handsomely. He agreed. His brother then brought a letter to Xiamen and gave it to my son Yangwang. After receiving the letter, my son came to Tong'an on the evening of the 26th and asked the 215th Regiment of the 108th Brigade of the 36th Garrison Division to send troops to retrieve me. Regiment Commander Liu Ying immediately sent a company of about 150 soldiers, led by the bandit who was entrusted to buy me and his brother. They arrived at Tianzhu Mountain before noon on the 27th. At that time, the bandits were out, and only two bandits were guarding me. The two people who reported the news fooled them and killed them. I was then rescued. At 3:00 PM on the 27th, I took a car to Tong'an and stayed at the house of my friend Ye Zibo," and so on. Zeng returned to Xiamen from Tong'an on the 29th and lived in his private house in Gulangyu, refusing to see guests. Because of the labor and fright of the 11th, he was old and sick. The officials and officials discussed that the bandits who helped Zeng and their brother each received a reward from Zeng. It is said that the bandits sent a letter to Zeng's family demanding 200,000 yuan in ransom, but now they were rescued by the official army. It was a great fortune in the misfortune. (March 30th)

Songjiang

Attempted Marriage Failed, Suicide Attempt 109

The Sen Tai Wood Shop outside the East Gate of this city, which has recently closed down, has an apprentice named Zhu Youquan, who is just a young man. He is from Pinghu. In recent years, he and a woman surnamed Dai and a woman named Xiaomeitou outside the East Gate have been communicating with each other and discussing marriage. However, the woman surnamed Dai must wait for a son-in-law to be recruited, and the family of Xiaomei is religious and does not marry outside the religion. Zhu Youquan asked his friend to mediate with both parties. As a result, the woman surnamed Dai was more affectionate, and Zhu Youquan was willing to be recruited as a son-in-law. He then sent a letter to his family in Pinghu to seek consent, but was rejected. Zhu Youquan believed that the marriage was blocked midway, and it was difficult for lovers to become married. He thought that the future was hopeless, so he borrowed money from a fellow villager and went to Shanghai to stay at the Oriental Hotel, secretly swallowing poison. Fortunately, Fang, an employee of the hotel, noticed something was wrong and asked him about the cause. He immediately asked a doctor to treat him. Fortunately, the poison was not strong, and his life was not in danger. He immediately sent a letter to his family to rush to Shanghai to pick him up.

###籌組兒童節紀念會 Preparing to Organize Children's Day Commemoration

As the nation prepares to celebrate Children's Day on April 4th, local educational institutions in this county are also actively making preparations. Yesterday, the County Education Bureau convened a preparatory meeting of various schools and institutions in the urban area, chaired by Hua Jinji. He reported on the proposed commemorative activities for this year's Children's Day, followed by a discussion and agreement on the following items: (1) The celebration assembly will include approximately one-tenth of the students from each school. (2) Each school will independently organize a propaganda team for mobile outreach. (3) Children will be encouraged to participate in exhibitions and sports meets organized by various social and educational institutions. (4) Entertainment venues will offer discounted admission to children, with tickets priced at twelve copper coins. (5) The presidium for the assembly will be composed of representatives from the County Party Headquarters, the County Government, and the Education Bureau. (6) The commemorative plan was approved as follows: A. A celebration assembly will be held at the Zhongnan Grand Theater at 9:00 AM on the 4th. B. Propaganda efforts will include posting slogans, organizing propaganda teams, and publishing a special Children's Day issue. C. Exhibition events will include a children's welfare exhibition, a children's domestic toy exhibition, and an achievement exhibition. D. Entertainment activities will include recreational performances, entertainment venues, children's health exercises, and the sale of children's products such as discounted merchandise, candies, and toys. Businesses will hang flags to show their celebration.

Confirmation of Gu Renfa's Bigamy; Prosecutor's Office Continues Interrogation 115

Since the Liu Zhuomin case, which implicated Li Shuyun, the wife of Gu Renfa, Director of the Civil Affairs Department of Jiangsu Province, the case of Gu Renfa's bigamy has caused a stir throughout the country and has been closely watched by people from all walks of life. This newspaper has reported on this matter in detail. It is now learned that the Nanjing Control Yuan dispatched personnel to Wuxi a few days ago for a secret investigation. Concrete evidence of Gu Renfa's bigamy has been discovered. The details are as follows:

Surveillance Committee Secret Investigation 116

On the 30th, the Nanjing Surveillance Committee sent a member and two secretaries to Wuxi for a secret investigation of the triangular relationship between Gu, Liu, and Li. After arriving in Wuxi, they used aliases and stayed at the Wuxi Hotel, keeping their activities very discreet. Few outsiders were aware of their presence. They purchased multiple copies of newspapers that had been reporting on the case in recent days for reference. They also went to the County Court to review Li Shuyun's statements. They left Wuxi for Zhenjiang that day, made a brief stop, and then returned to Nanjing. Gu Renfa has hired Qin Lianshan and Wang Youling as legal counsel for this case. According to Gu, he will go to Wuxi immediately when the summons from the Wuxi Court arrives at the provincial government. According to news from Nanjing, Gu sent a letter to Wang Zhaoming, President of the Executive Yuan, a few days ago, detailing the course of the case and requesting punishment. The letter was over a thousand words long.

Gu Confirmed to be Bigamous 117

Regarding Gu Renfa's marital relationship with his first wife, Ai Chengmei, Gu has claimed publicly that they separated long ago. However, according to reliable sources, Gu and Ai's marital relationship has not been terminated and is still in effect. This is proven by the household registration records of Nanjing City. The records state that at No. 3, Lane 3, No. 12, the following individuals reside: "Head of Household" Gu Renfa, alias Da'an, 43 years old, from Anlu, Hubei Province, moved in on January 30, year 23, currently serving as the Director of the Civil Affairs Department of Jiangsu Province, a graduate of the Japanese Military Academy; "Family Members": wife Ai, female, 42 years old, from Anlu County, Hubei Province; son Xinchan, male, 26 years old, studying at Hankou University; son Xinke, male, 8 years old; daughter Kaiti, female, 10 years old, studying at Nanjing Zhonghua Girls' High School; daughter Cixiang, female; female worker Song Wang; male workers Fu Guoliang and Cai Junchen; chauffeur Chen Zifang; Li Sanbao; cook Zhang Zhenxing, etc. Therefore, Gu's bigamy is beyond doubt. However, it is rumored that Gu and Ai have now reached an understanding, so Ai has refused to meet with reporters.

Zhenjiang Lawsuit 118

Regarding Li Shuyun's lawsuit against Gu for bigamy, it was originally intended to be filed in this county's court. However, after consultation between lawyers Zhang Shizhao and Chao Kun, it was decided that because a lawsuit against Gu for bigamy should legally be filed in the court where the defendant is located, a separate complaint has been drafted and submitted to the Zhenjiang District Court. Most of the evidence of bigamy is being collected from various sources by Li Shuyun's uncle, Li Wenhui. It is also heard that Li Shuyun demanded a divorce after discovering Gu's bigamy. After several negotiations failed to resolve the matter, negotiations broke down before Director Gu went to Jiangxi. To prevent Li from going to the Jiangxi headquarters to file a complaint, Gu sent several people to wait and dissuade her at the ferry terminal, which led to this incident. It is also heard that Director Gu always went to the Nanjing residence on Saturdays after completing his official duties and returned to Zhenjiang on Monday morning.

Continued Interrogation of Shuyun 119

Yesterday (the 31st) morning at around 9:00 AM, the Wuxi County Court Prosecutor's Office, after receiving the eight pieces of evidence related to the case sent by the Department of Civil Affairs the day before, ordered police officer Qian Chengjun, the chief prosecutor, to bring Gu Renfa, Li Shuyun, Li Liu, and Wen Rongzhen to court for questioning. Li Shuyun was questioned first and denied all eight pieces of evidence. She stated that she was willing to submit handwriting samples if necessary and requested that Gu Renfa be summoned to court for questioning so that the truth could be revealed. She also stated that she would accept legal punishment if there were any instances of selling official positions or titles. Next, Li Liu and Wen Rongzhen were questioned, and they also denied all the evidence and requested that Gu be brought to Wuxi for confrontation. The interrogation ended at around 10:00 AM, and they were all ordered to be returned to custody. It appears that this case will unfold further. The Prosecutor's Office, in order to understand the truth of the case, plans to summon all relevant parties for questioning one by one. Therefore, the day of confrontation between the two sides is not far off. The truth of the case will be revealed after the questioning and confrontation. Yesterday (the 31st), Shuyun's condition improved slightly and there was no major problem. She will soon recover.

Later, Hu was sentenced to life imprisonment by the Criminal Court, but Hu suddenly escaped from the bureau. Local communities, believing that there is a significant cover-up in this case, are requesting that the county and province conduct a thorough investigation.

Pig Vendor Zhao Dechun Robbed 121

Zhao Dechun, a farmer from Situmiao outside the West Gate of this city, in the Zhenbei Huayuan Village, who works as a pig vendor, was robbed. On the morning of the 30th, while travelling with a fellow vendor with 172 silver dollars, to Chenjiaji to purchase pigs, he encountered seven or eight robbers, each armed with wooden sticks and knives. They robbed all the money and stabbed Zhao in the foot before fleeing.

Another Car Accident on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway 122

On the Shanghai-Hangzhou highway, near the Ganpu station in Haiyan County, at 1:50 PM the day before yesterday, a private car with Shanghai license plate number 5427, driven by driver Huang Agui, was traveling from Shanghai to Hangzhou. As it passed the area, a local woman surnamed Yang, seeing the car approaching, tried to avoid it but was struck and injured in the head and waist, and her injuries were severe. The car, having caused a major accident, sped off towards Shanghai. Xieshi

Predictions for the Lantern Festival Competition 123

Xieshi lanterns have always been famous for their exquisite artistry, rarely matched elsewhere. In the past, when they were displayed at the Zhang Garden in Shanghai and on the banks of the West Lake in Hangzhou, they were admired by all. In recent years, due to the decline in the market, there have been no such events since the competition in the tenth year of the Republic. This year, various shops hope to revive the declining market with a grand attraction event. Initially, a few people proposed a white-haired lion dance competition, which coincided with the wishes of the shops, leading to a widespread response. The town's plan for a lantern festival competition has been decided by a joint meeting of the five towns, and organizers have been appointed to maintain order. Currently, thirty-five sets of pavilions and towers are under construction. The main lantern festival is expected to take place in late April of the Gregorian calendar. This year, various neighborhoods are exerting their utmost effort and creativity in crafting the lanterns, striving for even greater beauty. It is anticipated that the streets will be ablaze with lights, and the silver light will be dazzling, making it a spectacle to behold. It is also heard that the two railway bureaus have decided to run special trains for three days during the lantern festival. Yesterday, inspectors were sent to Xieshi to discuss locations for tourists to stop and watch.
