Women's World

Special Issue on Childrearing Problems

A Rational Solution to Childrearing Problems 286

— Yu Yuan

Traditional concepts passed down through generations tightly bind the hearts of the Chinese people, and the progress of most undertakings is only reflected in following the past and copying the old ways. Chinese villages still use the same production tools they have for thousands of years to make a living, and small-scale handicrafts and businesses in the interior are still stuck in their original processes. "Childrearing" naturally cannot escape the circle of inherited customs, and similarly falls into the trap of copying old methods without seeking innovation.

Of course, with the introduction of foreign civilizations, there are now more scientific methods of childrearing, and in fact there has been a belated implementation of childrearing, but this, just like other new undertakings, is only manifested in the upper-class lives of a few cities and among some intellectuals. At least, it is out of the question for the vast rural areas and the majority of the middle class who lack scientific knowledge. If we continue to work on the development of the childrearing cause in this way, it will still be of no help to the nation or to society.

Strictly speaking, the problem of childrearing is no longer a simple medical and infant education problem. Now, especially in China, which is urgently seeking national liberation, the problem of childrearing has become a social problem of considerable seriousness; it is related to the future of the Chinese nation and to the salvation and improvement of the lives of women. Therefore, childrearing is not just a personal or family matter, but should be a cause, and a movement, seeking a wider and more universal development. This is why we need to specifically propose "cooperative childrearing."

In the past few years, some people have proposed cooperative childrearing plans, but they have only been seen in theory, and they are still rare. As for practice, cooperative childrearing is naturally non-existent in the present, when all cooperative undertakings are still in their infancy. Our current need to promote cooperative childrearing is by no means to talk about a new theory to catch up with the times, and our purpose is certainly not for the convenience of a few upper-class lives and some intellectuals. We must promote the cause of childrearing with the dual prerequisites of national rejuvenation and women's liberation. Because: firstly, we believe that childrearing is not only personal but also social, so only the method of cooperative childrearing (pooling economic resources, hiring experienced and knowledgeable nannies, and raising children collectively) can achieve results. At the same time, only the method of cooperative childrearing can make it universal. Secondly, cooperative childrearing is much more economical in terms of cost than individual rearing. The success of cooperative childrearing can reduce the burden and pain of the vast number of working women and other vulnerable women. Thirdly, the realization of cooperative childrearing societies is also a partial success of women's liberation. Women engaged in social undertakings will not be affected by childrearing and affect their careers. Fourthly, we want to replace the old methods of the past with scientific childrearing methods, and only the method of cooperative childrearing can be effective. Because only a cooperative childrearing society is a reasonable and safe childcare center.

Looking at the current situation of childrearing in China, it can be said that it has become an obstacle to national rejuvenation and women's liberation. On the one hand, the infants themselves are mostly sick, stupid, and rude as a result of unscientific upbringing and spoiling or inability to love. How can such children not affect the future unsoundness of the country and the nation! On the other hand, it goes without saying that most vulnerable women feel the burden and pain of childrearing. Even women with better economic ability and higher intellectual level are often affected by childrearing problems, leading to their own unsoundness and the failure to develop their careers. These are all undeniable facts.

Therefore, we should strive to penetrate the knowledge of cooperative childrearing into rural areas, factories, small cities, and small towns, and widely popularize the organization of cooperative childrearing throughout the country. Those engaged in the women's liberation movement cannot lightly discard this problem; no one who is working for national revival can ignore this issue. We must do our best to seek a satisfactory solution and completion of the problem of childrearing in the practice of cooperative childrearing.

As for the aspects of the cooperative childrearing movement that should be carried out, here are a few points that may be briefly mentioned:

1. Cooperative childrearing societies are best organized by enlightened people in various places, taking the facts as the basis for the cooperative childrearing movement in each place. Then, to various counties, towns, and even villages.

2. Party departments at all levels, as well as local social education institutions and women's associations, should give the public a strong promotion and advocacy of cooperative childrearing in their respective locations.

3. Women's schools should add courses on cooperative childrearing.

4. Any movement, as long as you bury your head in doing it, do not sing high-sounding tunes, and do not shrink back, the completion of cooperative childrearing also depends on such people.

We further hope that the women's community will pay more attention to cooperative childrearing. And then get a bigger effect. Otherwise, simply shouting for the improvement of childrearing to the women's masses is tantamount to empty talk, and it is not enough to seek the realization of childrearing reform for only a very small number of people.

Childrearing Problems and Working Women 287

— Tong Hua

Childrearing problems can be divided into two points: one is the prenatal and postpartum recuperation of the mother; the other is the parenting methods after the birth of the infant. These problems are not a problem for wealthy families. Only working women who are whipped by life feel difficult and painful.

The daily nutrition and sufficient sleep of women are essential elements of healthy motherhood, and excessive labor and poor working conditions during pregnancy are not allowed to protect the mother and fetus. According to the general opinion of the medical community, women should have four weeks of rest before delivery and six weeks after delivery, because the uterus can only return to its normal state in the second month. Working too early often causes the uterus to droop, bleed, or become inflamed, or even cause infertility and mental illness. However, under the capitalist system, women have become wage slaves, and the intense, excessive, and unsuitable work for women has caused great damage to their bodies; insufficient nutrition and sleep have further deprived them of their health; generally, they only rest for five or six days before delivery, and after this, they must enter the factory to work, and life becomes a problem. Under these various ravages, the mother and infant cannot maintain their health and fall ill. According to a survey by Harpur Kings, among women of the European bourgeoisie, 9.17% suffered from miscarriage, and 9.85% suffered from stillbirth. Working women accounted for 17.89% of miscarriages and 32.57% of stillbirths, with the latter increasing three times compared with the former. From this comparison, we can also see the pain of working women.

Childbirth is a difficult hurdle for working women, but after passing this hurdle, the rearing of the infant is also a problem. The mother enters the factory, and the infant is thrown at home to starve and freeze, and the narrow and unclean living environment has a great impact on the infant's growth; as for the parents' lack of training in raising children,｜｜only emotion, lack of reason｜｜ also cultivates bad habits such as willfulness, greed, and selfishness in their children. In terms of education, working parents cannot talk about their children either.

X X X

In the Soviet Union, pregnant and nursing mothers are prohibited from doing factory night work. Before and after childbirth, mothers are entitled to four months of leave, with wages paid as usual. For six months after childbirth, female factory workers are entitled to an average of two hours of exceptional rest per day.

Children under the age of three are sent to nurseries at 7:30 in the morning, where caretakers manage the babies, arrange games in a scientific way, distribute food, and teach hygienic knowledge and collective consciousness. In 1929, 55,600 children entered nurseries in cities and industrial centers, increasing to 385,000 by 1932. In the main industrial sectors, more than 75% of female workers enjoy the convenience of nurseries. Other kindergarten education, public catering facilities, public laundries, public playgrounds for children, and social insurance are also developing day by day.

X X X

Chinese working women suffer even more than those in capitalist countries! Under the devastation of imperialism and feudal forces, factories in cities are reducing workers and closing down, and wages are extremely low. Malnutrition, insufficient rest; the Factory Law that stipulates that wages are paid for six weeks of rest before and after delivery is only a dead letter. In rural areas, natural and man-made disasters occur frequently, and farmers even use tree bark, mud, and wheat seedlings as food, so-called nutrition, so-called rest is even more out of the question, and mothers and infants have no way to maintain their health. According to the sixth issue of Zi Huan Monthly, the mortality rate of Chinese mothers is terribly high, with as many as 176 out of 1,000 people (in capitalist countries, it is less than this, with Denmark accounting for 2 per 1,000, Japan accounting for 3.33 per 1,000, Italy accounting for 3.37 per 1,000, the United Kingdom accounting for 3.38 per 1,000, Germany accounting for 57 per 1,000, and the United States accounting for 71 per 1,000). In terms of children, the mortality rate is also very high. According to Mr. Zhang Zhenzhi, "In various countries, 69 out of every 1,000 infants die, while in China, 50 out of every 100 people die, and in Hebei, as many as 75% die." The high mortality rate of mothers and children indicates the seriousness of the childrearing problem in China, and also indicates the bleak future of the Chinese nation! On this day of advocating the revival of the nation, if we do not seek to solve this basic problem, there will be no hope for the future of the nation, and I hope that the people of the country will pay attention to it.

A Brief Discussion on Children's Parasitic Diseases 288

— Described by Medical Consultant Chen Fangzhi

Parasites specifically refer to soft-bodied animals that parasitize the human body. Although tiny protozoa such as malaria and dysentery, and skin mites such as scabies and autumn lice, also parasitize humans, this term is usually not used. Therefore, the four words parasitic disease seem scary, but in fact the scope is very narrow; especially for children living in cities. There are not many opportunities for infection. Some parasitic diseases have local limitations. The parasitism rate is extremely small. So the scope is also narrowed accordingly. Now I will separately discuss the parts that are universal in urban and rural areas, and the parts that are limited to spreading in rural areas: Generally, those that are mostly transmitted through the mouth are more universal. Those that are not transmitted through the mouth, but through other routes, are mostly limited.

A. Parts that are universal in urban and rural areas:

1. Roundworms: The most commonly seen parasitic disease in children. This is the most common, and in places with the highest parasitism rate, this disease is often found in more than 90 out of 100 people. For children in Shanghai, according to the reports of inspectors, it is between 15% and 30%, which cannot be said to be small. The signs of onset are: pica. Good appetite. Nausea. Vomiting. Diarrhea. Or excessive sleep saliva. Abdominal colic. Systemic anemia. There are also reflex nerve-spasming symptoms. (Spasms, loss of consciousness, etc.) Come suddenly, parents think it is a serious illness, and the whole family is in an uproar, but in fact it does not matter much, and it can recover soon. Roundworms mostly parasitize in the small intestine. Generally, their eggs are brought in from unclean water and vegetables, etc., and hatch into larvae in the intestine, and after 30 to 40 days, they grow into adult worms, and can excrete eggs to the outside. To spread around. The medicine to expel them is "Santonin", the active ingredient of fresh Artemisia flowers, which is more effective. Ganji candy contains this medicine. Other marine algae and Quisqualis indica are also often effective, but Santonin can be toxic, so you must pay attention.

2. Whipworms: They are also widely distributed and often parasitize at the same time as roundworms. The parasitism rate is smaller than that of roundworms, and the symptoms of the disease are also lighter. In general, it is similar to roundworm disease. It is mainly characterized by persistent diarrhea and anemia. However, its parasitic site is in the cecum of the large intestine. The worm is 3 to 4 cm long, which is only one-fifth or one-sixth of the roundworm. The route of transmission is roughly the same as that of roundworms, with eggs being brought in from food and hatching in the intestine. Thymol is mostly used to expel the worms. But it often needs to be used in conjunction with enemas.

3. Pinworms: They are shorter and smaller than whipworms, only one-tenth of their size. They cannot be found in the stool unless you pay close attention. The eggs are also not as easy as roundworms and whipworms. The egg-checking method can be found with an ordinary microscope. So it is often difficult to diagnose. The parasitic site is in the rectum, not far from the anus, so the sick child often has anal itching or burning sensation, and after scratching, congestion and inflammation occur, which often causes sleep disorders. Apart from this, there are no other severe symptoms such as roundworms and whipworms. The way of infection is initially through food and drink, and then because of scratching the anus. The eggs are then brought into the mouth from the fingers, and the cycle continues, called self-infection. To expel them, garlic juice, or vinegar juice, or tannic acid juice is mostly used for enemas.

4. Tapeworms: There are intermediate hosts, which are cattle or pigs. If you eat raw beef and pork, you can sometimes be infected, but it is definitely not as common as the above three worms. The worm parasitizes in the small intestine. Patients often have abdominal pain, vomiting. Digestive disorders. Or abnormal digestion. High anemia, etc. The worm has sections, and the sections are connected, sometimes reaching 20 to 30 meters in length. The medicine to expel them is Dryopteris or pomegranate root bark, but they are all drastic drugs, and should not be taken casually.

Of the above four types, except for tapeworms, which are slightly dangerous, the other three types, after the patient is parasitized, only have repeated illnesses and pains, and there is no life-threatening danger.

(B) Parts limited to locality.

1. Hookworms. (or duodenal worms) They mostly invade the human body through the skin. Rural herdsmen and villagers. Are forced by their occupations. Expose their hands and feet. In order to come into contact with feces and fertilizers, it is the only way to get infected. Especially in areas where sericulture is flourishing, moist floating soil is suitable for their hatching, and infection with the disease is particularly common. After infection. Most fall into severe anemia, which over time can easily lead to bleeding, loss of appetite, and weak heart, often leading to death. The worm is only three or four cents long. It parasitizes in the duodenum. The medicine to expel them is mostly Thymol, or Dryopteris preparations.

2. Blood flukes: They also invade through the skin and parasitize in the hepatic portal vein, which can cause cirrhosis of the liver and endanger life. They spread to 13 provinces in our country, and there are many yellow-faced, big-bellied, and short-statured sick children in places where blood flukes produce a lot. But in large metropolitan areas. There is no chance of infection. Because of the lack of intermediate hosts. There is no way to expel this worm. It is more effective to kill it with needles and medicine.

3. Fasciolopsis buski: Xiaoshan County and Shaoxing County in Zhejiang Province are the most famous immersion areas. After its eggs are hatched, the larvae enter the intermediate host, the Planorbidae, and after asexual reproduction, they come out of the water and attach to aquatic foods such as water chestnuts, and children who eat them raw will be infected with the disease. Sick children often have developmental disorders. Or diarrhea, abdominal pain, anemia, and dysentery. The worm is as big as a thumb and shaped like a thin slice of ginger, hence the name. The medicine to expel it is mostly Thymol.

The above seven types are common parasites. The symptoms of other parasites, such as liver flukes, lung flukes, Trichinella, and filarial worms, are very different from what ordinary people call children's parasitic diseases; and these diseases are relatively rare. Therefore, they are omitted.

"Note" The symptoms inquired by Mr. Yu Jizhi of Jiangdu are definitely pinworms. If the mother and grandmother suffer from this, it is called family infection. Among parasitic diseases, only this pinworm disease has it. Taking too much deworming medicine. Of course, it is not suitable.

The Conflict Between Career and Motherhood 289

— Bi Yang

When discussing women's career issues today, it is already outdated nonsense to talk about whether women should or should not have careers, or whether they are suitable or not, from the standpoint of gender. The current demand of women for careers and their gradual acquisition of careers is an objective and natural trend of social development. The ancient saying of "men manage the outside, women manage the inside" has long been crushed by the wheels of the times. Therefore, when discussing this issue now, we should take an objective standpoint, experience its content from the actual career life, explore its essence, and then point out the path it should take.

Women of the middle and lower classes are increasingly feeling the difficulty of life due to the impact of the overall social downturn. Therefore, a large number of them have entered banks, companies, shops, and various vocational institutions in society to serve as employees, or as elementary school teachers. Women in the lower classes have no choice but to enter factories in large numbers, sell their labor, and even sell their bodies, due to the pressure of life. Even those married women, although many of them regard marriage as a "nursing home," in fact, not only is the income of men alone insufficient to maintain life, but also in this present society with many unemployed people, not every man has a career, and even those who already have one are constantly living in terror of the danger of unemployment, so they have no choice but to leave their families, abandon their children, and run to society to find various careers. The increasing number of female teachers, female workers, and female employees is a fact.

Modern women's careers, from their own point of view, although they have given women the opportunity to be economically independent and break away from parasitic life, on the other hand, the burden of family chores and raising children has not been reduced in the slightest. Especially the work of raising children makes working women feel an indescribable pain! Working women of the upper class can still hire nannies and maids to raise their children, but working women of the middle and lower classes rarely have this possibility. As for those working women who "do one day and eat one day," life is a problem, let alone hiring a nanny or maid to take care of their children. Therefore, in any country, the mortality rate of children in worker areas is always more than twice as high as in other places.

Working women are forced by life to solve the problem of eating first, and put the family and raising children in a secondary position. When the work is over, they run home exhausted and have to breastfeed and raise children and deal with all the family chores. Therefore, the career and motherhood conflict, and the life of working women is burdened with another layer of heavy burden, and at the same time, their spirits are also increased by another layer of pain!

But how can we avoid this conflict and resolve this contradiction? Of course, we cannot, like Ms. Ellen Key, see that the career is harmful to motherhood and fundamentally advocate that women return to the family and regard raising children as their natural duty. This is not only a method of "throwing away the baby with the bathwater," but also impossible in reality. We should try to remedy this harm from the career itself, turn family chores into social undertakings; hand over the work of raising children from the hands of mothers to the hands of experts, and turn it into a part of social undertakings, so as to avoid the conflict between career and motherhood, and to thoroughly eliminate the burden and pain of working women!

○ ○ ○

The Importance of Nurseries 290

— Nourishment

Nurseries are already very popular in the Soviet Union, providing most people with immense convenience and satisfaction. Now, some people in China are advocating for the establishment of pilot nurseries. However, many have expressed opposition, believing that taking children away from their loving mothers' arms and entrusting them to strangers is akin to sending them to foundling hospitals or other charitable institutions for upbringing. This is because they do not understand the nature of nurseries. Now, I will briefly describe the nature and importance of nurseries below:

(1) Children Receive Scientific Care: The organization of nurseries cannot be compared to foundling hospitals in China. The most important aspect of establishing nurseries is to pay special attention to children's health and education. Therefore, the facilities of nurseries must be very complete. Nannies must receive special training. All work outlines should be determined by experts in children's affairs, doctors, nurses, psychologists, and others. After the decisions are made, they should be published in newspapers so that the general public can participate in discussions. Then, after review by children's affairs experts, they should contribute their own theories and experiments to determine a system. All management policies of nurseries are based on scientific explanations given by physicians regarding the necessary physical functions of children. Children with illnesses, regardless of severity and type, are sent to children's hospitals or clinics for diagnosis and treatment. In addition to these nurseries, there should also be experimental nurseries. This is because it is felt that knowledge and methods of caring for young children require thorough research and improvement. Therefore, this experimental institution is specifically established to accommodate ordinary children, allowing the most excellent child experts to research new methods to raise children.

(2) Reducing Obstacles to Women's Economic Independence: It is undeniable to people with clear minds that women should be economically independent. However, for women who have been bound by families for thousands of years, the most difficult problem to solve when they want to leave their families and participate in social undertakings is that there is no one to take care of their children. Because of this problem, many women abandon their careers and return to their families to raise their children. Therefore, people who oppose women's careers often use this fact to resist and as an excuse. If there are well-organized nurseries in society, then working women can send their children to the nursery from seven or eight in the morning and pick them up again in the evening. In this way, mothers' work will not be affected by their children, and the biggest difficult problem for women seeking economic independence will naturally be solved.

According to the above-mentioned facilities and educational methods in nurseries, they are more complete and harmonious than general family childcare. The people who care for the children are experts and must have good training and knowledge. Therefore, parents can absolutely rest assured that sending children to nurseries can receive modern scientific care methods. And this method is by no means the "children are owned by the state" that ordinary people rumored, which completely cuts off the relationship between parents and children. After work every day, parents can still bring their children home and share family happiness. Women demand economic independence and gender equality, but they are often constrained by children and burdened by trivial family matters. If this system can be adopted, it can at least be said that it is the beginning of women's liberation.

Hoping for Nurseries 291

— Bai Li

The poorer people are, the more they fear having children, but children come even faster.

I am nearly six months pregnant, and worry and annoyance are growing in my heart day by day. I feel that this is a major problem.

Under the pressure of life, my husband and I have to go to work separately to make a living. In the near future, we will have to take leave to await childbirth, and the source of income will have to be borne by him alone. Saving a little, there will certainly be no problem before childbirth.

What I find most difficult is the problem after childbirth. Hiring a wet nurse would require providing her with housing and meals, which we, who barely make a living, certainly do not have the spare capacity for. Breastfeeding myself would mean ending my future, as I would not be able to go to work, and life would be unimaginable at that time. However, this is the only way.

"Can't we have a nursery?" Our group of economically independent women often hopes for this. Indeed, if there were a nursery, I could send my baby there and pay a reasonable price each month, which would be of great help to me! I can still work, without being subjected to the pressure of life, and provide the child with a well-trained body.

I remember a friend telling me that there is a nursery in Shanghai, which was said to have been founded by people from the Shenbao newspaper. By paying twelve yuan per month, your child can live safely inside, and they hire professionals to take care of the children very thoughtfully. - But I inquired with others and everyone said they didn't know. I wonder if there is really such a nursery established to seek happiness for us working women?

I am looking forward to it.

I cannot give up my career, and at the same time, I cannot abandon this future little citizen.

I deeply look forward to it: before the child is born.

Editor's Note:

The Shenbao newspaper does not have a nursery. However, the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association does have a plan to organize a nursery, which is currently in preparation and will soon be officially established.

Questions and Answers about Diseases 292

Answer to Mr. Huang Ruilan from Bengbu.

Question: Chest pain with shortness of breath. According to your letter, it is probably a stomach ailment. It started one or two months after conception, and is related to pregnancy-induced acid reflux. Taking Chinese medicine cured it, which means the acid reflux period has passed. Afterwards, the dates of the pain became closer, which may have caused a real stomach ailment. This cannot be clarified by letter inquiry. Arsenic acid can sometimes lighten skin color, but it is a highly poisonous substance. Do not take it indiscriminately without a doctor's guidance.

Ode to the Congress of the Chinese Medical Association

Delighted by this clear and harmonious day,

Locust flowers bloom all over the courtyard.

Huainan becomes a city of learning,

A spring terrace is obtained on the river.

Reviving the country relies on spreading secrets,

Seeking mountains, hence coming from afar.

Let us gather under the trees,

And continuously hold Li Ying's cup.

Early Summer of the 23rd year of the Republic, Written for

The Grand Occasion of the Congress of the Chinese Medical Association Respectfully Wishing from The National Federation of Physicians

Congratulatory Message from the Shanghai Medical Association 294

On the occasion of the Chinese Medical Association's meeting in the capital on April 1st of the 23rd year of the Republic, as bright spring days gather gentlemen in one hall, how magnificent! Truly a grand spectacle. Medicine is a matter that emphasizes both academics and profession. The purpose of our association is to protect the profession, while the gathering of your association relies even more on promoting academics. Separated, the efforts are divided and dispersed; united, the efforts are concentrated and focused. This is why the unity of the two associations is necessary. Therefore, based on this meaning, we offer this message:

The meaning of the association lies in unity,

Academics and profession must be combined.

If one is lacking,

Like riding without reins or a car without tracks.

Magnificent congress gathers in the capital,

Unveiling essence to amaze the ignorant.

Knowing that on the day of return,

It is the time of spiritual unity.

Respectfully wishing from the Shanghai Medical Association

The Significance of the Chinese Medical Association Holding a Congress Zhu Hengbi 295

Medical congresses in Eastern and Western countries are extremely grand events. They have the encouragement of the government and the welcome of society. The number of attending physicians is at least several thousand, and often exceeds one or two thousand. New medicine in our country has a small number of people, and the scale of each congress is far inferior to that of advanced countries. However, in the past twenty years, there has been considerable progress. I still remember that at the first congress of our association, only a few dozen people attended. At the last congress, there were over five hundred people. The number of registered attendees at this congress has exceeded the number of the last congress. At the first congress, there were only a dozen or so papers, and many were urged by telegram. Even if the content was slightly inferior, it was included in the agenda to fill the length. There was no distinction between internal and external departments. Now, the number of papers submitted to each department is increasing daily, and those that arrive later can only be reluctantly abandoned and not used. Moreover, there are many subjects, and the division into groups for discussion has reached as many as eight categories: internal medicine, surgery, obstetrics and gynecology, public health, dermatology and venereology, radiology, pathology, and physiology. During the congress, experts gather in one hall to question and debate. The benefits can be summarized as follows:

(1) Building a car behind closed doors cannot lead to conformity. This is true of everything, and science is no exception. Using one's own achievements for others to scrutinize, if there are any shortcomings, it is not difficult to discover them. This is the first benefit of the congress for individual academics.

(2) Academics are public property of the world. Anything gained should be published openly, breaking the bad habits of secretiveness in old medicine for thousands of years, so that academics are not treated as private property. This is the second benefit of the congress for the population.

(3) As far as we know, there are often research experts who compile the results of their daily work into volumes, and over the years, they cannot find their way through them. Now, urged by the congress, they must be busy organizing them. Thus, what was previously buried in the laboratory can now be organized and completed and made public to the world. This is the third benefit of the congress, which can promote the organization and rectification of research materials.

(4) When the congress is about to open, everyone competes to submit papers. Those who were previously lazy in research will now want to show their skills. Those who have always liked research will also double their efforts. This is the fourth benefit of the congress, which can encourage researchers.

(5) There are thousands of members in our association, scattered all over the world. Usually, they only exchange news and information through letters and magazines, and it is often difficult to speak their minds freely. Now that there is a congress, members from all over the east, west, south, and north gather in one place to discuss the improvement of the medical community and the promotion of public health. This is the fifth benefit of the congress, which can gather wisdom and benefit extensively.

(6) General assembly affairs, without a congress, would have incomplete reports, and motions may not be fully implemented, leading to neglect. Now, with this congress, staff members cannot but double their efforts, each seeking to be worthy of their position, and the association's affairs are progressing rapidly. This is the sixth benefit of the congress, which benefits the association's affairs.

In summary, it can be seen that although the congress program has only a few chapters, each word and sentence represents the crystallization of the thoughts and efforts of thousands of members over the past two years, and is not accidental. After the closing of the congress, the members of our association will return to their original places, taking their gains and continuing to study them in order to deepen their knowledge. During the closing period, they will work, and during the congress, they will report on their work and discuss it openly. The cycle continues endlessly, and progress is made without limit. It is not like ordinary congresses, where resolutions are not made or implemented. Therefore, although the members of our association hold a congress only ten times in two years, the spirit of research has never been diminished even for a single day. At this time, when the number of members is not very large, a congress every two years seems to be enough. In the future, as the association's affairs develop and the number of people increases, it will inevitably be held annually. If there is too much research material and it cannot all be included in the annual congress, then it will inevitably be necessary to hold small-scale local meetings, or as the number of specialized talents increases, in addition to the congress, there will also be specialized congresses. There are already physiological congresses, pathological congresses, etc., and the implementation of departmentalization is a beginning.

In short, the more scientific conferences there are, the greater the contribution to academics. All the papers solicited at each congress of our association are published in the Chinese Medical Journal. At the beginning of the journal's establishment, it was bilingual in Chinese and English, with four issues per year. Now, Chinese and English are divided into two sections, with twelve issues each per year. The original works contained therein have gained high praise from the medical community at home and abroad. Our association has more than 1,700 members, one-third of whom are physicians from various countries in the East and West. This kind of mixed academic group is only seen in other countries, and it can be said that it can practice the meaning of academics without international boundaries. This congress is held in the capital, and we are grateful for the hospitality of the authorities, the support of academic groups, the encouragement of the press, and the benefits of discounted train fares from the Ministry of Railways. It can be seen that all sectors of society in our country have high expectations for our association. Our colleagues can only work harder to live up to the expectations of the people.

The Association Has a Major Mission Pang Jingzhou 296

(Members Have a Major Responsibility)

The Chinese Medical Association, in its past history and present reality, in addition to academic research, is indeed also involved in research on business, medical education, health administration, and all issues within the scope of medical affairs.

The association itself is formed by gathering medical colleagues from all over the country, so it has more unity and national character than any other organization.

Precisely because it is an association formed by gathering colleagues from all over the country, it should have the vision and insights to see all parts of the country.

Therefore, in this transitional era of the new China, I think the focus of medical improvement is still on several associations, and each member simultaneously bears a significant responsibility. Therefore, the words, actions, and thoughts of each member have a major impact on the future of Chinese medical affairs.

When the association holds a national congress, it is especially an opportunity for each member to fulfill their responsibilities. Therefore, I would like to ask each member to always keep in mind the improvement of Chinese medical affairs, and especially to pay attention to the exchange of views between colleagues in one place and colleagues in other places, so as to obtain a kind of standard that is suitable for the whole country.

Although there is more than one medical association in China now, since most members can exchange views in one meeting and obtain good directions, then why can't two associations exchange views in one country and obtain more appropriate solutions?

Members fulfill their responsibilities in the meeting and seek the improvement of Chinese medical affairs, and they must have the common goal of all people, and they must have a comprehensive vision. The two associations jointly seek the improvement of Chinese medical affairs, and it only lies in the words, actions, thoughts, and vision of each member.

Dear members, please always be mindful of your position, which has the authority to influence the entire Chinese medical community.

The Chinese Medical Association is holding a congress in Nanjing, and the Shenbao is publishing a special issue. Jingzhou was asked to write an article, and Jingzhou respectfully uses these words to wish all members attending the congress good health and success.

Prospects for the Association's Future Work Song Guobin 297

The Chinese Medical Association is holding this congress in the capital for the second time since its merger with the Bo Medical Association. I am fortunate to be able to participate in this grand event. The association's work in recent years can be seen from Mr. Zhu Hengbi's article "A Review of the Past Year," which shows the intensity of the work and the remarkable achievements. Everything that I had hoped for from the National Federation of Physicians has been fully realized by the association, which is truly in line with the conditions for the survival of the group. I would like to briefly present a few points based on my thoughts as a supplement to the association's future work, which I hope will be approved by the members:

(1) Proposal to Establish a Medical Research Institute: The research institute is the highest academic institution in the country. Regardless of the type of science, those who want to explore its profound realm all rely on the establishment of the research institute. Since the government established its capital in Jinling, it has paid attention to education and professions in the country, and thus the Central Research Institute was established. All disciplines in the arts and sciences have everything they should have, but medicine, the crystallization of science, is still lacking. Because of this, medical school graduates in the country and returned students from overseas want to continue their research, but they suffer from a lack of appropriate institutions. Academics have no end, and the key lies in continuous research. Now that there is a lack of this kind of research institution, advanced medicine is stopped midway, and those who love learning go against their wishes. Old knowledge is feared to be neglected, and new knowledge has no hope of creation. This is regrettable. Our association is the highest academic institution in the national medical community. It seems that it should take the stand of promoting academics and take the important measure of saving academics, urging the government to add a large-scale medical research institute within the shortest possible period and within a possible range, so that the students will not be abandoned midway, and the prosperity of medicine may be able to rival Europe and the United States. This is the first.

(2) Preparation of Draft Regulations for Physicians: The government has formulated and promulgated regulations for various industries, accounting for seven or eight out of ten. However, regulations for physicians have not been promulgated to this day. In the past, the National Federation of Physicians, in the name of the congress, telegraphed the government, urging it to promulgate them as soon as possible. However, those who spoke earnestly were ignored by those who listened. Is it because the government is busy with other matters and has no time for this? Or is it because there is a shortage of talent to formulate these regulations? If the regulations for physicians are not formulated effectively, then the rights of the medical community cannot be guaranteed. Although the government can treat this indifferently, it is an urgent matter for our medical community. I believe that many of the members of our association are practicing physicians in the country, and there are probably not a few who are well-versed in the law. Instead of sitting and watching the government delay and fail to promulgate this regulation for a long time, it is better for our association to gather this talent, collect this material, examine the established rules of various countries, and take into account the current situation in the country, and formulate a "Draft Regulations for Physicians," and then submit it to the government for adoption and implementation. Since it is based on the opinions of the majority, it can avoid the criticism of being contradictory and inappropriate, and the government can also achieve twice the result with half the effort. The formulation is by the association, and the promulgation is by the state, which seems to be different from overstepping one's authority. This is the second.

(3) Recommendation to Increase Internship Time in Medical Education: In the past, I had the recommendation of "hospitalization of schools" and "hospitalization of schools." The purpose of medical education is twofold: one is to cultivate advanced scholars, and the other is to produce treating physicians. In terms of academics, the former should not be taken lightly, but in terms of practicality, the latter is even more important. Practical science is different from those who only engage in empty talk, so academic experience and academic experience cannot be lacking, and experience is especially important. In recent years, there have been many medical schools in the country, but few of them meet the principles of medical education. Most ordinary medical schools do not have affiliated hospitals, and even if there are one or two with hospitals, the period for students to practice in the hospital mostly begins two or three years before graduation. It seems that such a short period of internship is difficult to achieve any effect. After graduation, when they come out into the world, there are many cases where they are unable to clarify their doubts during diagnosis. In my opinion, the internship time in the hospital should be extended to at least four or five years, so that the effect of emphasizing both theory and experience can be achieved, which is in line with the principles of medical education. The trial period is limited to the time of schooling, and after starting a practice, it can never have the slightest experimental nature. Our association pays extreme attention to the issue of medical education, and recently there has been the establishment of a committee to standardize the curriculum of medical schools. If we can focus on this purpose and extend the length of hospital internships, so that medical school students have sufficient experience in treating diseases after graduation, it may be of help to the future of medical education. This is the third.

(4) Compilation and Translation of Medical Books: In recent years, the government, considering the difficulty of purchasing foreign books and the need to promote the national language first, has issued a general order to all schools in the country, regardless of the type of science, that those who use foreign original texts as textbooks should all be replaced with Chinese texts. Only in medicine has it not been possible to achieve the effect of popularizing Chinese textbooks. This is because medicine is the most profound specialized science. If all textbooks are to be translated into Chinese, then it is necessary to engage in the translation of foreign books. Most of the medical translations published in the country are superficial. Therefore, the schools that use the original texts are still countless. Our association is aware of this, and has worked diligently on the compilation and translation of medical books in recent years. However, in my opinion, the scale is still too small. If we can expand its scope and, to the extent of our financial resources, employ specialized translators to engage in large-scale compilation and translation, then the results will certainly be amazing, and the benefits will be indescribable. The dispute among medical factions is due to the different languages and texts of foreign students. Now, if we translate the medical books of various countries into Chinese and set them as textbooks, then the languages and texts will be unified, and where will the differences of opinion come from? Moreover, the original books of Europe and the United States are of particularly high value, which is beyond the reach of poor families. If there are Chinese translations, then everyone can have one. For the association, it can also be associated with this great work and become immortal. Nothing is more important than the survival of the spirit. This is the fourth.

The achievements of the association in recent years are clear for all to see, and those who know them cannot but praise them. This is not only my "unbiased opinion." The above-mentioned points are just my humble opinions and one-sided views. Judging from the association's usual spirit of doing things, they should also be easy to do.

Preface to Physician Pang Jingzhou's Journey North Yu Yunxiu 298

Xu Shu Chong's "Shuowen Jiezi" says that sheep are in groups, dogs are alone, dogs get along and fight, so the word "group" follows sheep, and the word "alone" follows dog. I have often silently observed the Chinese people, who lack the virtue of being in groups and have more individualistic nature. In a country, whether it is a large government agency or a small alley, if three people form a crowd, there will be the problem of collusion and friction. At first, it involves things because of people, and then it goes against the public and becomes private. Therefore, since the Revolution of 1911, for more than twenty years, there has been chaos and turmoil, the country has not been established, and it has been shrinking by a hundred miles every day. This is the effect of being alone. Being in a group means being united, and being united means having strength. Strength is enough to shoulder great and difficult responsibilities. Being alone means being divided, and being divided means having weak strength. Weak strength means being unable to do anything. Scientific medicine in our country is just beginning to sprout, and its momentum has not been consolidated, and its strength has not been enhanced. Metaphysics hinders its progress, bad habits disturb its rear, the knowledgeable above destroy it, and the ignorant below slander it. Danger and doubt are intertwined, and obstacles are piled up. It is appropriate to unite rather than divide, and it is appropriate to be in groups rather than be alone. This is obvious. However, those who talk about medical factions in the world often say German, Japanese, English, and American. Although this is the talk of ordinary people, when it is actually examined, those who are involved use languages that do not communicate with each other, and the generation of divisions is naturally not surprising. It is not about having the view of superiors and subordinates. However, impetuous and frivolous sons use it to indulge in their mutual struggle, and eventually lead to separation and division, and develop into factions. They are eager for the small benefits of sharp knives and slow to consider the fundamental and overall plans. It cannot be said that they are not extremely foolish. Whenever I talk to Pang Jun about this, I cannot help but sigh and hate it. Last autumn, I also tried to find ways to communicate and unite with Niu Jun Huisheng and Xu Jun Naili. Before the plan was hidden, the matter failed to be completed, which is also what Pang Jun and I deeply regret. Investigating the reason for this, it is that over the years, there have been frequent instances of surpassing, but the sincerity of integration has not been fulfilled, which has led to this. Therefore, if you want medicine to be in a larger group, you must connect with sincerity and trust, support each other, reverse the previous mistakes, and it will not work. Pang Jun's journey north is to inspect schools above the professional level by order of the Ministry of Education. Pang Jun is in the wild, and his medicine is in Germany. He has been to England, France, the United States, and Japan, and has no partisan heart in his chest. Moreover, he hopes that medicine will be in a group, and he hopes that those who are alone. The Ministry of Education has many virtuous talents, and there are also many people who know medicine, but they only take Pang Jun, so what is their intention? Then, what I have been lamenting about, can I rely on it to make up for its regret? Pang Jun, please work hard to do it. Moreover, I have something more to say. It is inevitable that academics will have factions. Where there are factions, there will be struggles. However, if the struggle is in academics, then the research will inevitably be more diligent, and the exploration will inevitably be more precise. The progress of virtue and the cultivation of business both rely on struggle. If the struggle is in power and profit, then the jealousy will inevitably be more severe, and the exclusion will inevitably be more intense. The heart of changing, deceiving, and hating will be born with the struggle. It is to kindle its group. I think that the academics that have factions can still maintain their old habits. There is no need to change them, and there is nothing that can be unified. As for the administration of government affairs, it should be governed by the degree of equality and fairness, so that people can find a way to be effective in the country, and there is no fear of rumors and concealment. If they shift their competitive minds to academics and maintain their peaceful spirit in politics, then perhaps the struggle is not in gain, and their individuality can be in a group. I ask Pang Jun, what do you think? On his departure, I will take these words as a gift.

The Experience of Applying Analgesics 299

By Physician Li Qingchao

Nowadays, when it comes to analgesics, everyone praises morphine and salicylic acid for their strong and rapid pain-relieving effects. However, morphine has a strong narcotic effect, which can damage brain nerves and easily lead to addiction, even chronic poisoning. Salicylic acid, when used in large quantities, often causes adverse side effects, such as tinnitus, palpitations, and sweating. Thus, the patient's suffering is not relieved but rather precedes with unpleasant sensations. I often see ordinary people, when attacked by pain, either inject morphine or take opium, hoping for temporary relief, but disregarding the future dangers, eventually leading to deep poisoning and becoming incurable. Medicine is meant to treat people, but now it kills them instead. Is this the original intention of medical professionals in using drugs? Therefore, searching for an analgesic drug that has the special effects of morphine but without the drawbacks of addiction and brain damage is an urgent task for today's medical professionals and is also eagerly awaited by the masses!

Since the advent of "Veramon," pain sufferers who previously groaned in bed and tossed and turned in restlessness have been able to relieve their pain in a very short time. The speed of its analgesic effect is truly unbelievable. "Veramon" not only relieves the patient's pain but also provides the patient with considerable convenience: because this medicine only needs to be taken orally to show its effectiveness, there is no need to ask others to inject other dangerous analgesics.

We must know that localized pain can affect the health of the whole body. For example, a sore throat can make it difficult to swallow, and a toothache can make it impossible to chew, which can hinder nutrition and cause indigestion. Then, gastrointestinal diseases will follow, so how can we ignore it! "Veramon" can easily treat toothaches and sore throats caused by tooth decay and pharyngitis. Insomnia is also most likely to damage the mind because the cause of insomnia may be headaches, neuralgia, or earaches, etc., just as the saying goes, "If one meridian is not in harmony, the whole body is not comfortable." If "Veramon" can be used to relieve pain, you can naturally fall asleep peacefully. In this case, "Veramon" indirectly protects our health. Women experience an extra layer of pain due to their unique physiology, namely, pain during menstruation and labor pains during childbirth. I still remember a woman in labor who had severe labor pains but did not want an injection, so she was given "Veramon." As a result, the labor pains were greatly reduced, and the delivery was not affected in any way. In recent times, morphine and its derivatives have been abandoned for pain when suffering from diseases in the urethra because they can sometimes increase pain. If the dosage is slightly larger, it can easily cause unpleasant side effects such as vomiting or nausea. Therefore, the most appropriate method of pain relief at this time is to use "Veramon." For pain after surgery or bone fractures, gallstone, kidney stone pain, stomach pain, etc., no matter how severe, "Veramon" can immediately stop it, and its effect can last for several hours. This is something that other pain relievers cannot compare with!

The Essentials of the Telecommunications Industry

National Defense and Telecommunications 300

— Lü Bing

Since our country has been subjected to active aggression by foreign forces, the whole country, from top to bottom, has gradually shifted its gaze to the borders and deeply feels that in this trend, without consolidating national defense, there is no way to establish a nation. The so-called gradual encroachment and division all start from the frontier and extend to the Central Plains. The importance of the border is definitely no less than that of the inner regions.

During the January 28th Incident, after the arduous struggle of the National Army, the war of resistance lasted for a month, and its achievements were remarkable. At that time, the unity of the people and the dedication of the soldiers were the main reasons for the victory, but transportation and communication equipment were also crucial. At critical moments, the staff did not hesitate to brave danger to establish contact, so the military authorities were able to调度指挥 and fully facilitated. International official communication also reached far and wide, winning deep sympathy. This kind of duty was originally what those who served in transportation should do, and there is no need to elaborate more. However, judging from this, we can see the importance of the relationship between national defense and telecommunications. Therefore, speaking of national defense today, if we consider it beyond our reach, we should first develop transportation, and in the development of transportation, the construction of roads and the communication of telecommunications are equally important.

Roads are not within the scope of this publication, so I will not discuss them for the time being. As for telecommunications in our country's northwest and southwest borders (the southeast coast focuses on coastal defense, but our country also has a northeast border, but it is pitiful to mention, as it has already created a puppet state), it can be divided into wired and wireless telecommunications. In terms of wired telecommunications, the line from Beijing via Zhangjiakou and Kulun to Buyantsogt (Kyakhta) is used to connect with Mongolia. The line from Lanzhou via Suzhou to Turpan is divided into two routes: one via Dihua to Yili and Khorgos, and the other via Yanqi to Kashi and Irkeshtam, both of which are used to connect with Xinjiang. The line to Qinghai goes from Lanzhou via Pingfan to Xining, and then connects with Huangyuan and Guide; the line to Xikang goes from Hanyuan in Sichuan Province to Kangding. In addition, the border of Yunnan Province goes from Tengyue via Xiaoxin Street to Bhamo in Burma, and from Hekou to Lao Cai in Annam. The border of Guangxi Province goes from Nanguan to Lang Son in Annam; the border of Guangdong Province goes from Dongxing to Hanoi in Annam. This is the general situation. In terms of wireless telecommunications, Yunnan and Xinjiang have radio stations. Other places such as Tibet, Mongolia, and Qinghai still lack additional installations. Judging from this, the communication related to national defense should be vigorously developed in line with the needs; otherwise, if there are many troubles in the border areas and news is delayed, how can we cope with them with ease?

Developing the Northwest and consolidating national defense requires this determination. Looking at the newspapers, the central leaders have successively disregarded fatigue, traveled to the border areas, and conducted on-the-spot investigations, so future achievements will definitely be considerable. However, in terms of telecommunications alone, given the vast territory of our country and the length of the borders, the cost of laying wired telecommunications is high and the project is huge. Wireless radio stations can be regarded as a communication tool, and it seems appropriate to start with their construction first. However, the establishment of radio stations in the border areas also requires a lot of money. Given the current shortage of telecommunications funds, how can it be done quickly? It is heard that the initial plan of the Ministry of Communications has been implemented to increase equipment in Lanzhou as a western communication center and to establish radio stations in Suiyuan, Zhangjiakou, and other places to connect with various places in the southeast. This measure will provide considerable convenience for communication in the Northwest, but it cannot be said that this construction alone is satisfactory. It is believed that the development of the Northwest border areas concerns the national economy and the people's livelihood. The development of water conservancy and farmland, the planning of roads and transportation, all require funds. A comprehensive plan should be formulated, and a portion of the funds should be designated for the equipment of communication. In this way, once the foundation is laid, success can be expected. As for the fact that the Northwest region is vast and sparsely populated, desolate and undeveloped, and people in the interior consider it a long journey, it is heard that the Ministry of Communications has already formulated reward regulations, and all personnel who go to work in the border areas will be given preferential treatment beyond the norm. This shows that the Ministry of Communications pays attention to border communication and has a predetermined overall plan. It is hoped that the whole country will cooperate and actively participate. It must be known that developing border transportation and exploiting Northwest resources is also a way to consolidate the national defense gateway. Looking forward to the future of our country, this is indeed the urgent task at present.

The True Meaning of Telegraph Price Reduction 301

— Sun Yi

Recently, the Ministry of Communications stipulated that "the name and address of the recipient of each telegram, up to 15 characters, will be calculated as 5 characters." For the sender, the savings seem to be very little; but for the Ministry of Communications, the resulting loss is quite considerable.

Originally, the price of telegrams in China was much more expensive than in Western countries. Because it was too expensive, the general public would not send a telegram unless they encountered extremely important matters. The communications authorities understood this, so they wanted to try their best to reduce the price. However, in this period of extreme shortage of telecommunications finances, if the price of telegrams were reduced to the same level as in Western countries, it would simply be impossible to maintain it. In desperation, they came up with this alternative solution: reduce the cost of the recipient's name and address. Although it cannot meet the hopes of the general public, it is much more convenient than before!

The telecommunications industry (including wired telegraph, wireless telegraph, city telephone, long-distance telephone, and wireless telephone, etc.) has a very close and important relationship with a country's politics, military affairs, culture, education, economy, finance, and all industries and commerce; and its principle is nothing more than facilitating the people. Therefore, this kind of business is run by the state, unlike ordinary industries and commerce, which are solely for the purpose of making profits. Even if there are times when it loses money, it must still be operated as usual. However, in Western countries, the government subsidizes this kind of business from the national treasury every year, only seeking the development of the business and achieving the purpose of facilitating the people; it does not need to haggle over every penny. Therefore, the competent authorities can feel at ease to engage in it and strive for development; even if the price of telegrams is lower, it will certainly not affect the business itself. At the same time, on the other hand, once the price of telegrams is lower, the public will naturally be happy to use them; sending a telegram is almost the same as the cost of sending an express letter, and the speed of telegram transmission is much faster than that of letters. In this way, the use of telegrams will naturally be widespread; since the use of telegrams is widespread, the telegraph business will naturally develop; since the telegraph business has developed, even though the price of telegrams is low, the losses can naturally be compensated.

However, our government has never subsidized the telecommunications industry. Not only has there been no subsidy, but in the past era of warlords, they arbitrarily appointed bureau chiefs, exploited telecommunications funds, and regarded the telecommunications bureau as a tax revenue agency, and the pain still lingers! Even now, the official military telephone bills owed by military and political organs are no less than more than three million yuan per year. According to the statistics of national telecommunications revenue and expenditure, there is a surplus every year; in reality, there is a deficit every year. This deficit is affected by the official military telephone arrears. In recent years, due to bandit disasters and wars, the original lines have been severely damaged; and telecommunications funding is very exhausted. Not only is it impossible to expand telecommunications construction, but it is already extremely difficult to maintain the original business!

Not long ago, telecommunications colleagues, due to the shortage of telecommunications funds, in order to maintain the status quo, once had a proposal to increase the price of telegrams. The reasons are as follows: Postal rates have already increased from three cents and four cents to five cents; train ticket prices have also increased much more than before. Postal services, railways, and telecommunications all belong to the transportation industry; moreover, postal rates will never be subject to arrears from military and political organs; although railways are sometimes affected by free tickets, the losses will certainly not be as much as telephone bills. Postal rates and train ticket prices can still be increased, so why can't the price of telegrams be increased? However, after repeated consideration by the Ministry of Communications, not only was the proposal to increase prices not adopted, but ways were also found to reduce them. The motivation is nothing more than to make the general public feel the interest in sending telegrams, so that they will not regard telegrams as "inauspicious objects" as before. This plight should be seen by all Chinese people!

This method of the Ministry of Communications is really a helpless measure due to the shortage of telecommunications funds. If the domestic politics is on the right track and the arrears of official military telegrams are properly resolved, the price of telegrams will definitely be gradually reduced. We know that the current telegraph bureau is no longer like the yamen of the past! The personnel working in the telegraph bureau are no longer like the bureaucrats of the past! The speed of telegram transmission and the accuracy of the text have also improved much more than before! Sending a telegram can indeed get the benefit of a telegram, and it will never be like the telegrams of the past, which were sometimes slower than letters. If everyone can feel the interest in sending telegrams and everyone can make full use of telegrams, then the telecommunications business will naturally flourish, and the industry and commerce will gradually prosper! This is the true meaning of the telegraph price reduction!

Telecommunications Miscellany丨Telephone丨Automatic 302

— Guan

Calling it "It Says Through" is Really "Not Through"

Those who use automatic telephones pick up the receiver, hold it to their ear, and at the same time use their hand to dial the number they want to call. The previous article mentioned something called "Reachable and Through," the sound of which, like machinery, is considered to mean that it can be reached; however, sometimes after hearing the sound of "Reachable and Through," perhaps after dialing, there will be "Hatred, Hatred," intermittent and melodious, buzzing. The sound of "Hatred, Hatred" undoubtedly expresses a kind of regret. "Hatred, Hatred" is technically called "Busy Tone." "Busy Tone" is really not through! Why is it through but not through? The "Hatred, Hatred" sound emitted by the machinery is exactly like notifying the user there, that is, "The user you want to call is busy talking to someone else and must wait a while before you can reach them."

From this, before an automatic telephone call is made, you always hear a through sound (the sound of machinery). The sound of the through is not the same, and whether the telephone can be connected or not is also distinguished by hearing a "Reachable and Through" or "Busy Tone." (Shared telephone also has "Busy Tone," so the operator can avoid saying "Line is busy.")

As for how the machinery in the telephone局内 emits the sound of "Hatred, Hatred," this should also be what ordinary people who do not understand the situation of automatic telephone wiring want to know. In short, (detailed wiring will be discussed later) automatic telephone machines, depending on the user's own dialing, the machinery in the局内 responds and acts. As for dialing wiring, after the user dials an Arabic numeral, the machinery immediately selects an idle line from the lines belonging to this group and connects it to the second group. When the second number is dialed, the machinery also selects an empty line, so as to connect it to the third group. In this way, it is pushed forward layer by layer to connect to the required user. If the empty lines in a group have already been completely occupied by the user, or the user being called has already been connected and is talking to someone else, then the machinery used to select, in one transfer, is not connected to the busy line, but is connected to other machinery. Through the action of this machinery, it emits a special sound wave, so that those who dial the phone at this time hear the sound of hatred...hatred...unceasingly. (The sound of hatred, hatred can be stopped, just put down the receiver.)

According to Telephone丨Automatic, the first article was published in the second issue and was temporarily suspended due to the crowding of manuscripts. It is not that it will not be continued. This is specially attached to answer those who ask. In the future, as long as the position allows, I will continue to write.

European Telephone Paradise丨Sweden 303

— Chen Xianding

Using the Telephone丨Novel Method

Europeans often call Sweden the telephone paradise. The Swedish Iron Industry and Commerce Association recently wanted to hold an executive committee meeting using the telephone. The meeting had a total of six representatives. In addition to the chairman residing in Stockholm, the capital of Sweden, the other five people lived in various cities. Some of the cities are up to 500 miles apart. According to the ordinary method, they must gather in the capital, which takes many days. Now they can use the telephone to discuss 会务. During the discussion, each representative can hear the arguments of the other representatives and can speak in turn. It saves time and reduces costs. The method is quite novel and practical. According to Mr. Neom, the chairman of the association, "When the meeting is held, the discussion is the same as sitting around the table." Its convenience can also be imagined.

According to Mr. Hult, an engineer at the Swedish capital telephone局, who implemented this plan, the plan has been successful in theory. Once the tests are completed, the procedures for preparation can be simplified a lot. The stipulated method is as follows: Before the meeting, you must first contact the capital telephone局 to settle everything. There are no restrictions on call time on Sundays and holidays. On other days, it is stipulated that the limit is 15 points. The call fee for each participating representative is slightly higher than the ordinary long-distance call fee. However, the call fee between the Swedish capital and major cities is US$0.26 (equivalent to 7 角 8 分 in Chinese currency) every three minutes during peak hours. Fifteen minutes is only US$1.30 (equivalent to 3 元 9 角 in Chinese currency), which is not too expensive. Moreover, you can enjoy half price before 9:00 am and after 6:00 pm. If the distance is shorter, the call fee is also relatively reduced. From the Swedish capital to Lapland in the far north, the journey is about 900 miles, and the call fee every three minutes is only US$0.65 during the day and US$0.30 at night.

Sweden's novel use of telephones is not limited to "telephone meetings." If telephone users in the Swedish capital are unable to answer the phone in person due to going out for business, whether it is for a few hours or a few weeks, they can request the局 to connect all calls to a dedicated telephone operator, record the numbers of all calling users one by one, and, if necessary, instruct them to answer the phone on their behalf. When the user returns home, they can receive a list of the calling user numbers and the communication records of the phone calls that were answered on their behalf. The fee is also very low, only US$0.025 per call.

The Understanding that the Social Community Should Have of International Wireless Radio Stations (Part 2) 304

— Chen Tianzuo

Speaking of Diplomacy

In conducting diplomacy, countries, in addition to negotiating and competing at the table, also use telecommunications to achieve publicity effects as a diplomatic tool. It goes without saying that they use international telecommunications to exchange information with foreign embassies and consulates; they also use international telecommunications to stir up international public opinion and shift the world's attention to achieve diplomatic success. I still remember that during the Washington Conference, the Shandong issue became the focus of the conference. The debate was unprecedentedly fierce. The whole nation paid attention, and their joys, sorrows, and emotions all depended on information; and appeals and petitions, as diplomatic support, also relied on telecommunications. Fortunately, at that time, the American Pacific Water Line Telegraph Company was able to quickly transmit this telegram, so that information was agile and the situation could be dealt with properly. International communication's convenience to our country was also a powerful force in achieving some results at the Washington Conference. If the conference were not in the United States at that time, and international communication was not autonomous and was controlled by others, the result would be even worse, as expected. Now that the international station has been established, there is no need to worry about others strangling our throats. This is how the international station is related to our country's diplomacy.

Speaking of Military Affairs

When international wars occur, a country's international communication agency is the target that the enemy country wants to destroy first. The right to use international submarine cable communication in our country is entirely in the hands of foreigners. Once something happens, this traffic tool will not be used for our benefit, and we will not be able to contact our allies in a unified manner, and we will inevitably become a major flaw in the international war barrier! Even if there is superior international submarine cable communication, it is still useless without a strong naval force to protect it. Because submarine cables are laid on the seabed, stretching for thousands of miles, separated by oceans, and difficult to protect, it is wise to build an international station as a national defense communication agency under the current state of our country's weak naval power. Because it does not occupy a large area, military defense is easier to implement. Now that the international station has been established, as long as there is a considerable air force to protect it, there is no need to worry about the interruption of international communication when international wars break out. This is how the international station is related to our country's national defense.

The relationship between the international radio station and our country's economy, diplomacy, and military affairs is as described above. What is the result of its business? This should be said urgently. The most important conditions for the transmission of telecommunications are speed and accuracy. The machinery used by the station all uses the latest high-speed automatic transmitting and receiving machines. Transmitting and receiving telegrams are all done by machines, not by manual labor, so its maximum speed can reach about 300 characters per minute. As for direct lines, it can reach New York and London, the financial centers of the world, as well as major cities such as San Francisco, Paris, Berlin, Geneva, Moscow, Manila, Java, Saigon, and Hong Kong. The fastest transmission time per message is only one minute. In terms of accuracy of transmission and reception, the station has assigned specialists to carefully proofread incoming and outgoing plain and encrypted telegrams. Therefore, in the past three years, the station has transmitted and received more than 10 million characters of telegrams, of which only more than 10,000 characters were wrong, with an average error of only 1/10,000. The reason is that the station colleagues deeply know that most international telegrams are related to business information. A delay of one second or an error of one word is crucial to business gains and losses, and the input and output are extremely large, so they are all careful and sensitive. As a result of the station's hard work and progress in the past three years, the business situation has developed day by day. Now domestic and foreign financial institutions, import and export merchants, news agencies, and embassies and consulates of various countries in China are competing to have their international telegrams transmitted by the station, which shows the public's firm belief in the station, and the station's increasing business is not accidental.

Furthermore, the decline of our country's international status is an undeniable fact, but to improve our international status, we must work together consistently to show something. In the past, when international communication agencies had not been established, we had to endure the pain of allowing the overflow of rights and interests when communicating with overseas messages. Now the international radio station has autonomous rights, and its relationship with military affairs, diplomacy, etc. is as described above, and its business performance can also be so rapidly improved. If people in society send international telegrams and abandon the autonomous international radio station, how can patriots bear to do this? I dare to tell you frankly, in order to seek the public's understanding of the station, and to encourage the station to make further efforts.
