Telecommunications World 306

— Fang Zhen

American Wireless Facsimile Telegraph

An American wireless company, recently approved by the Washington Federal Radio Commission, is launching ultra-shortwave facsimile wireless communication between New York and Philadelphia. The equipment for this communication is currently being rushed into production. After these two locations are connected, the business will be expanded to Chicago, Washington, Boston, New Orleans, San Francisco, and other major cities. Photos and letters can be transmitted and received using radio waves as long as five meters. Moreover, specially made multiplex equipment can be used to send three telegrams simultaneously on one wavelength, with a maximum speed of 180 words per minute. The telegram charges will be calculated based on the size of the image or letter. The price will be lower than ordinary telegram rates. The aforementioned ultra-shortwave radio stations planned for these locations are scheduled to open for communication in June of this year. At that time, it is also planned to connect with the company's international wireless circuits to send and receive international telegrams.

Recent Situation of British Telephone Services 307

According to the British Post Office General Accounting Department, the postal services of the United Kingdom generally showed a downward trend in the fiscal year ending March 1932, but a glimmer of hope appeared in 1932-33. Although parcel post was 151,666,000 items in 1932-33, less than 158,100,000 items in 1931-32, it has shown an upward trend since March 1933. Significant increases between 1913-14 and 1932-33 are as follows: Telephone calls increased from 834,000,000 to 1,490,000,000. Telephone exchanges increased from 2,900 to 5,300. Unemployment insurance increased from £1,560,000 to £36,180,000. Letters increased from 5,783,700,000 to 6,640,000,000. However, domestic telegrams decreased from 75,618,000 to 36,041,000. (Report from the American Consul General in England)

Quick to Succeed 308

Bi-Monthly News 309

— A Club Member

Dispatching of Telegraph Lines

The dispatching of wired telegraph lines is closely related to the speed of telegraph services. If the lines are dispatched properly, the telegraph services can be exceptionally fast. Recently, the Ministry of Communications has been dispatching telegraph lines in various provinces based on the local telegraph service conditions. The important ones are recorded below:

(1) Shanghai Qingjiangpu has been using the Western Union telegraph machine for direct communication since March 22nd. After that, telegrams between Jiangbei and the Shanghai-Hangzhou area should be particularly fast.

(2) The direct Pinghan (Beijing-Hankou) telegraph circuit was interrupted for several years due to the telegraph wires between Shunde and Zhangde being destroyed by the military during the war. The Ministry of Communications has now completed the repair of the wires between the two places and ordered the Pinghan bureaus to restore direct communication.

(3) Telegrams between North China, Central China, and South China used to be relayed through the direct Jiujiang-Guangzhou circuit, which was quite fast. However, since the Communists occupied Gan province, the direct Jiujiang-Guangzhou line has been blocked. In order to provide relief, the Ministry of Communications has ordered Hengzhou, Hunan, and Guangzhou to open direct communication. At the same time, additional wires will be installed between Changsha and Hengzhou to open direct Yuehan (Guangdong-Hankou) communication.

(4) Telegrams between Shanghai and Jiaxing and Jiashan used to be relayed through Suzhou. Now, direct communication has been established since March 19th.

(5) There are many telegrams between Tunxi, Anhui, and Shanghai. However, they currently have to be relayed through the Wuhu and Nanjing bureaus. In order to expedite telegrams between Tunxi and Shanghai, the Ministry of Communications has ordered the Wuhu Bureau and the Shanghai Bureau to communicate directly, so that it is not necessary to relay through Nanjing.

Improving the Method of Telegram Delivery by Messengers 310

Major city telegram bureaus and telegraph offices often receive more than 1,000 telegrams per day. Therefore, each messenger usually carries four or five telegrams to deliver in sequence. This not only wastes the messenger's time waiting in the bureau, but also delays the delivery of the last telegram. In order to provide relief, the Ministry of Communications has ordered busy bureaus and offices to dispatch messengers to deliver telegrams as soon as they arrive, with the principle of messengers carrying fewer telegrams and returning to the bureau early. At the same time, more messengers will be added to gradually change to one messenger per telegram delivery, so that incoming telegrams can be exceptionally fast and not delayed at all.

Amateur Weekly

The Municipal Election Issues We Should Pay Attention To 311

— Gong Pu

The Shanghai Municipal Council election of the Public Concession has recently concluded, and the representatives elected by the Chinese Ratepayers' Association's Citizens' Group were also announced a few days ago. Amidst the election voices of both the Chinese and foreign sides, two phenomena have been discovered. The reporter believes that these two phenomena are worthy of in-depth discussion, and they are first raised in this issue, and then studied in detail in subsequent issues. How to promote and advance the basic issues related to municipal progress and the cultivation of preliminary civil rights is something that all citizens and party and government authorities in this city should pay close attention to.

(1) Regarding the first phenomenon, before the foreign directors of the Municipal Council were produced, Mr. A. W. Beanmont, the editor of the English "Minle Weekly," published an article criticizing the Municipal Council election, saying that the Shanghai municipality was controlled by a certain underlying force. The reporter has not yet found Mr. Beanmont's original text, but according to the general idea recorded in various newspapers, Mr. Beanmont's statement is shocking, but it is true. Mr. Beanmont believes that "...... because he witnessed that the corruption of the Shanghai Public Concession municipality is absolutely incomparable to the municipal progress of major cities in the world, this reason is due to the lack of municipal progress thinking of Shanghai citizens, but the municipal power has always been controlled by a certain underlying force, such as the re-election of the Municipal Council directors every session, often the candidates are designated by a certain underlying force, and their names have already been drafted, so the voting of citizens is just a formality. Therefore, the so-called Municipal Council directors are ultimately nothing more than directors or managers of major foreign banks, figures in the pockets of wealthy Jewish merchants...... Because they are all important members of a certain association and claim to be a special class in the concession, so people say that the production of Municipal Council directors comes from association elections rather than city elections, which is indeed true......" Whether his words are groundless is really worth studying.

(2) The second phenomenon is that the Chinese Ratepayers' Association represents the will of Shanghai citizens and is an agency for the welfare of Shanghai citizens. Shanghai citizens should pay very close attention to the election of the Ratepayers' Association. However, according to newspaper records, the number of people with the right to be elected in this Chinese election was more than 3,000, and the number of people with the right to vote should be several times or even dozens of times greater than this number. However, the result was that only more than 2,000 votes were cast. This phenomenon not only shows the weakness of the general public's municipal concept, believing that the quality of the municipality cannot be controlled by themselves, but also the indifference to elections is even more significant.

Speaking of the content of these two phenomena, regarding Mr. Beanmont's belief that the biggest reason for the corruption of the concession municipality is the control of a certain underlying force, and that the "lack of preliminary civil rights thinking" of citizens is secondary, the reporter's opinion is different from Mr. Beanmont's. Because we know that the corruption of the municipality is indeed due to the control of a small number of "special classes," but why can a small number of special classes control it? Then we have to blame the Shanghai citizens' neglect of elections. If every citizen with the right to vote in Shanghai can actively participate in the election and pay close attention to the candidates, how can a small number of special classes still manipulate it? Therefore, the reporter believes that the only important reason why a small number of special classes can control it is that citizens do not take the municipality seriously, and even less take the election seriously. Under this circumstance, it is not easy to eradicate a certain underlying force.

Secondly, speaking of our own side, it is not only that the above-mentioned indifference is even worse than that of Westerners, but also the fear of foreigners is even more obvious. Because the concession has always been managed by Westerners, the general public has long believed that they have no right to interfere, and also believe that Chinese directors are just a formality and have no real power. Little do they know that one aspect of our country's being invaded by foreign countries is indeed the inevitable demand of imperialists, and our own self-abandonment, weakness, and incompetence, which have enabled foreigners to make progress, is also a great reason. Therefore, one of the biggest reasons for the lack of progress in the concession municipality can also be said to be that our citizens do not pay enough attention to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association and the election of representatives, and cannot do their best to support the Chinese directors. Therefore, although the Chinese directors have always been outstanding members of society, their contributions are still limited, and they cannot do their best to seek welfare for our citizens, and cannot do their best to fight against foreigners. Directors must be constantly encouraged by citizens and do their best to support them, so that they dare to do things boldly. Now that the majority of citizens are indifferent to the directors, they have no power to do things, cannot be valued by foreigners, and naturally cannot talk about the courage to resist.

In short, if we want politics to be on the right track, the people must truly be able to supervise politics and participate in politics; if we want the people's participation in politics to be thoroughly realized, we must first be able to actively promote, cultivate, and implement the preliminary work of civil rights with one heart and one mind from top to bottom. Looking at the election situation of both the Chinese and foreign sides this time, what is most touching is that Westerners who are familiar with democratic politics, and Shanghai citizens who have gained more new ideas, still have such a weak understanding of elections. From this, we can imagine the civil governance ideas in the inland provinces of our country.

Today, people in the government often make grand pronouncements about democratic politics. We sincerely do not know how to start democratic politics in this current situation, and how much promotion and cultivation work the promoters of democratic politics have actually done. This is an associated feeling that we must have when we begin to discuss the Shanghai issue!

Rebuilding Houses 312

— Jiang Wen Gui

"Old X! These houses here really look unreliable!" It was a bright morning, and the residents of XX Alley were all discussing this in whispers.

The truth is this: The houses in XX Alley have been around for twenty years. Although the exterior doesn't look very old, the interior at least presents an old appearance: the roof beams are a bit skewed, and the floors are a bit rugged.

The news of "rebuilding" had been spreading throughout the alley for two or three days, but because it was unofficial, it was just suspicious speculation.

Yesterday, a message came from a restaurant at the entrance of the alley, saying that the landlord had definitely decided to demolish the houses here. The reason why it could attract the attention of everyone in the alley was because the small boss of the restaurant was a close friend of the landlord. Today, the situation has completely changed. All you can see in the alley are piles of people discussing it widely. It seems that the situation is much more tense.

Finally, one hour after the meal, the landlord's notice was announced. This undoubtedly caused panic and astonishment among everyone in the alley. Involuntarily, everyone in the alley lost their courage, and all the previous discussions disappeared.

At first, an old gentleman from a cigarette paper shop initiated a union. He first discussed it with the hotel owner next door and settled on it as a temporary meeting place, and then found an old distillery owner to help. Then, they began to proceed.

A union needs to gather talents, so their first step was to contact the tenants. The stores in the front have successively received their notification, but the rows of residences inside are not within their sphere of influence. Contacting them is not as easy as they thought, but they have to contact them.

Among the rows of residences inside, the more reputable ones can be considered the elementary school principal and a veteran and capable Mr. Zhu. Because they are both intellectuals, people's faith and worship of them can be easily grasped.

Of course! In order to consolidate the union, these two pillars are indispensable. Therefore, they are responsible for the work in the residential area.

Around six o'clock in the afternoon on the first day, the union was established in such a vague manner. The hotel-style auditorium was crowded with the giants of each family, all showing a bitter face that was neither crying nor laughing. In fact, at this time, there was nothing to laugh at.

Each family has its own situation, and each person has his own difficulties. After this small group was produced, who doesn't want to complain? Needless to say, this small auditorium has already become quite deafening.
